Page 12

The Movement to Overthrow the Japanese Cabinet Has Not Ceased (Japanese Correspondence) 99

The Crisis of the Seiyukai

The Current Cabinet's Difficult Situation

Everyone knows that the turmoil in Japanese politics has a historical background. This historical background is particularly serious in Japan, namely, the international crisis publicized by the general public, the crisis of 1936, the rumors of a war between Japan and the United States, the rumors of an inevitable war between Japan and the Soviet Union, and recently the added deterioration of relations between Japan and the United Kingdom. The Japanese General Staff is naturally particularly busy, and the Army and Navy are also preparing and rapidly expanding their military equipment. The more urgent the expansion of military equipment, the more intense the atmosphere of social unrest.

Originally, the Saito Cabinet was a so-called "national unity cabinet" during a period of emergency. Once the emergency period was over, things should have returned to normal. In fact, the so-called emergency period, from the perspective of Japan's actual situation, was mostly internal. As such, the Saito Cabinet should have resigned long ago because of its own unsoundness. However, it unexpectedly lasted until now. The Navy Minister, Foreign Minister, Army Minister, and Minister of Commerce and Industry have been replaced, and now the Minister of Education, who comes from the Seiyukai, is also involved. In the past, Okada, Uchida, and Araki all resigned on the grounds that their ill health could not withstand the pressure of work. Only Nakajima Kumakichi was questioned by the House of Peers about the "Ashikaga Takauji Theory," which harmed the Japanese national essence, and was forced to resign. In fact, the resignations of the past ministers all contained serious contradictions in Japan's domestic and foreign affairs. The so-called "illness" was indeed a pretext. From this method of filling cabinet vacancies, one can know the characteristics of the emergency cabinet, and also glimpse a part of the recent changes in Japanese politics.

Whether the Saito Cabinet will collapse after this depends on the strength of the overthrow movement, and at the same time, it depends on how they use their political skills. According to the past situation, it was not as if people did not express dissatisfaction with the Saito Cabinet, and it was not as if they did not consider the Saito Cabinet to be too weak and powerless. However, they were unable to overthrow it. The strong cabinet that the military expected was difficult to produce, and a party cabinet could not be brewed. The reason for this is that the military is not very unified internally. The Navy and the Army have different political views, and within the Army, the Araki, Masaki, and Ugaki factions stand in a three-legged balance of power, unwilling to yield to each other. Therefore, the Hiranuma Cabinet has become a thing of the past, and I am afraid it will never be realized again. Secondly, the representatives of the elder statesmen, such as Prince Saionji, quite disapprove of the military's actions and are unwilling to lightly allow the military to form a cabinet. A party cabinet cannot happen because the credibility of the parties has been lost and cannot be restored in an instant. This time, the bribery case of Minister of Education Hatoyama, as exposed by Okamoto, although the facts may not necessarily be correct, has greatly damaged the parties. It is almost impossible to restore constitutional order.

Moreover, the current internal situation of the Seiyukai is similar to that of the Kiyoura Cabinet era. The opposition between Tokonami, Kuhara, and the executive faction is extremely sharp. Because of the issue of the violation of party discipline by Mr. Tsugumo Kunitoshi and Mr. Nishiho Riba, the internal conflicts of the Seiyukai have been caused by the issue of expulsion. Tokonami Takejiro's opposition and Mochizuki Keisuke's cautious remarks have put the current executives in a dilemma. Since problems have occurred in the party's control, they have involved the entire parliamentary politics.

Hatoyama Ichiro and Mitsushi Chuzo are both current cabinet members from the Seiyukai, and they are all key figures involved in the issue of discipline. What the truth is is another matter. This alone can agitate the feelings of the general public, expose the stains and weaknesses of the current government, and the military can take advantage of it to create a military fascist politics. Kuhara's faction, since it is at odds with the executive faction of the Seiyukai, will use any means to overthrow the current cabinet. They secretly collude with the Kokumin Domei, unite dissidents, and concentrate their efforts to attack the weaknesses of the current government. At the same time, they also plan to contact Tokonami's faction to oppose the executive faction. Their steps are: first, return the expulsion order; second, impeach the impropriety of the executives expelling members of parliament from the party; and third, propose a motion of no confidence in the president. Of course, during this period, there will be movements in various localities and in the parliament to support the current executives. Under the opposition of the two sides, the ugly appearance of the parties will naturally be exposed even more severely. The military will increasingly use this dispute to carry out the overthrow of the cabinet. However, the practicality of the military's monopolization of politics in the future is still immature. The form of parliament can still be extended for a certain period of time. (Tokyo, February 23)

Post-War Problems in Southern Fujian 100

Seven Route Soldiers Disarmed and Transferred North

Civil Army Commanders Ordered to Be Abolished

Xiamen Correspondence, The military situation in Fujian Province, since the reorganization of the 19th Route Army into the 7th Route Army, has been completely stabilized after the entire force was transferred north to Henan for training. When the 19th Route Army gathered in Hui'an, Putian, and Xianyou, there were still nearly 30,000 people. Among them, some wanted to break through the encirclement and go to Longyan to gather and form an army. However, the Central Army's defenses were very tight. Except for the 61st Division's Shi Baoqi Regiment, about 600 people who escaped from Tuling in Hui'an to Jiudu in Nan'an and were recruited by the civil army Chen Yucai, the rest were unable to break through or were intercepted. As a result of discussions between Wei Lihuang and Mao Weishou, the 60th, 61st, 78th, and 49th divisions were disarmed before being transferred north and then departed. As a result, the 60th, 78th, and 49th divisions in Putian and Xianyou were disarmed by the 36th Division in Hanjiang, Putian, in early February and transported north by ship. The armaments were handed over to the 36th Division for safekeeping and transported to Beijing by another ship. The 61st Division was finally disarmed by the 10th Division in Hui'an on the 12th and transported to Beijing from Tuling and the 7th Route Army headquarters on the 20th. After the soldiers of the four divisions were disarmed, they were reassembled under the supervision of the Central Army. The newly appointed division commander gave a speech, saying that disarming was not surrendering and that the meaning was absolutely different. Because the current position and environment of each division were very bad, the soldiers were colluding with outsiders to sell firearms privately or fleeing in groups, which would be tantamount to trapping the soldiers in crime. Therefore, at this time, the arms were temporarily confiscated and the order to depart was followed. After arriving at the training location designated by the Military Commission in the north, the firearms would still be returned to the soldiers. The Central Government had absolutely no discrimination against the 7th Route Army, and in the future, it would definitely be treated the same as the Central Army, etc. Mao Weishou came to Xiamen from Quanzhou on the 16th. He originally intended to ask for six months' leave, to be acted upon by Zhao Jinwen, the Chief of Staff of the 7th Route Army. However, Chairman Chiang sent repeated telegrams urging Mao to go to Ganzhou and commended him for his proper handling this time, and did not allow him to ask for leave. Mao flew from Xiamen to Shanghai on the Shanghai-Guangdong plane on the 22nd and transferred to Ganzhou to meet Chiang.

On the Longyan front, the entire Huang Renhuan Division of the Guangdong Army left Longyan on the 18th and withdrew to Shanghang and Wuping. On the one hand, Chen Jitang telegraphed Nanchang to ask Chiang to send a team to take over Longyan, and Chen also ordered all troops entering Fujian to withdraw to Guangdong before the 24th. The entry of the Guangdong Army into Fujian came to an end.

After the end of the military operations, the biggest post-war problem was the disposal of the civil army, especially in southern Fujian, which was the most complicated. Chairman Chiang had issued an order to all civil army commanders and military commissioners to abolish them all. The original order stated, "The military operations of this anti-rebellion have come to an end. The anti-rebellion civil army commanders and military commissioners appointed by this headquarters should be immediately abolished. This headquarters has appointed Yang Fengnian as the commander of the southern Fujian anti-rebellion army, Huang Kesheng as the deputy commander, Du Qiyun as the military commissioner, Yu Chengyao as the commander of the anti-rebellion army in Quanzhou and Xinghua, Song Yuanyuan as the special commissioner of Fujian pacification, Zhang Xiongnan as the commander of the anti-rebellion army in Yongde, Xiao Shuxuan as the military commissioner of this headquarters, Fang Shengtan and Lin Zhiyuan as the Fujian military commissioners, Shen Chichang as the commander of the Second Route guerrilla anti-rebellion army, Wang Changqi as the deputy commander, Lin Shouguo as the southern Fujian military commissioner, and Xu Youlin as the commander of the Fujian anti-rebellion civil army, and Luo Weixiong as the deputy commander. It is hoped that these officers will be ordered to comply with the abolition and report. All official seals, etc., should be cut off." Among those listed in the order, in addition to the military commissioners, all the commanders, only Shen Chichang, the commander of the Second Route guerrilla anti-rebellion army, belonged to northern Fujian, and the rest belonged to southern Fujian. In addition, there was also Qin Wangshan, the commander of the Jin-Nan-Hui anti-rebellion army appointed by the northern front headquarters, and the evil Deputy Commander Wang Zhennan. Among the civil armies, the one under Yang Fengnian in southern Fujian was the largest. According to the list he made, there were 30,000 people in Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, and Xinghua. After the Central Government issued an order to end the civil armies, Commander Chiang telegraphed Chen Yi, approving the reorganization of Yang's troops into two regiments of the Security Corps, with Yang as the commander. However, recently, when the troops were reviewed in Zhangzhou, the troops in Zhangzhou alone had reached ten battalions, about 6,000 people. The number will be reduced to six battalions and reorganized into two regiments. However, Zhang Wende, Zhang Xiongnan, and Lin Jing in Quanzhou still have no less than 7,000 or 8,000 people, and there is no way to accommodate them. Zhang Zhen, the former commander of the 49th Division, once went to Quanzhou for this matter and met with Wei Lihuang to discuss the results. It was proposed to ask Chiang to further reduce the number of security teams in Quanzhou by two regiments. Commander Chiang telegraphed Zhang to Nanchang to discuss the matter of the reorganization of the civil army in southern Fujian in person. Zhang plans to fly to Ganzhou after meeting with Chiang Dingwen in Xiamen today (23rd). It is heard that Qin Wangshan's troops will be reorganized into one regiment, with Wang Zhennan as the regiment commander. As for the bad troops, they will all be disbanded. Those who disobey will be treated as bandits. The Wu Ci Department of Du Qiyun's Department is now being suppressed by the Third Division. (February 23)

After the National Army Captured Yongxin 101

The People Who Have Been Communist-ized for Seven Years are Returning One After Another

The Headquarters Orders Strict Prevention of Bandits Destroying Bunkers

Nanchang Correspondence, The Headquarters announced that the National Army's advance into Yongxin, occupation of Longyuankou, and recovery of Yongcheng only used a few regiments of troops to fight fiercely against the pseudo 18th Division, pseudo independent regiment, and Red School student team. The bandits resisted stubbornly with danger, and the National Army fought bravely, one falling, another following. It was only possible to kill the enemy and achieve results. Since the occupation of Qixicen Longyuankou on the 5th and the recovery of Xincheng on the 18th, the time was not long, and more than 5,000 people have returned. Yongxin has been communist-ized for seven years, and so many people have returned, which is truly a manifestation of the total collapse of the Jiangxi bandits.

Also, after the Red bandits were strictly blockaded by the National Army, the materials in the bandit area were extremely panicked. The bandits were most panicked by the National Army's construction of bunkers, so they came up with ghostly tricks and specially made a kind of iron-covered vehicle, about two feet high, with iron plates as a cover, under which two or three people could be hidden. They held iron drills, cauldrons, chisels, and other things to rush to the foot of the bunker, and then used iron drills, cauldrons, chisels, and other things to destroy the bunker. After the headquarters reported the investigation by the Special Investigation Office of the Provincial Party Department, it divided the orders to the various armies and the provincial government to quickly install auxiliary defenses in the bunkers everywhere to prevent peeping, and to manufacture anti-strike equipment to bomb and destroy the car. It is learned that after receiving the order, the City Defense Headquarters has specially transferred the order to its subordinate military and police agencies to follow. (February 26)

Zhang Xueliang Arrives in Hankou 103

Scheduled to be Sworn In

And Will Inspect Bandit Areas

Hankou Correspondence: Zhang Xueliang, Deputy Commander of Bandit Suppression for the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, arrived in Hankou on the 23rd aboard the Yong Sui warship from Nanjing. On the 24th, it passed Wuhu, Anqing, and Jiujiang. On the 25th, he arrived in Hankou at 8:30 AM. Chief of Staff Qian Dajun, Chief Counselor Xia Douyin, Pacification Director He Chengjun, Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun, Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the Hunan-Hubei Border Region Xu Yuanquan, Garrison Commander Ye Peng, Commander of the Second Naval Fleet Zeng Yiding, and others, leading civil officials of the rank of Jianren and above, and military officers of the rank of Major General and above, welcomed him at the Sanbei Wharf. Amidst tight security by the military and police, Zhang went to the Bank Association's office to meet with military, political, party, provincial, and municipal party committee representatives, and gave a speech, roughly stating, "I have received orders from the Central Government to reluctantly take on the position of Deputy Commander of Bandit Suppression for the three provinces. I will do my utmost to wipe out the remaining bandits and stabilize the local areas. The organization of the headquarters will remain the same, with no changes whatsoever, and no additional deputy commander headquarters will be established to save expenses. The date of my inauguration has not yet been set. I intend to begin work first. To understand the bandit situation, I will personally inspect the areas." When Zhang set off, the National Government sent Secretary Gao Lingbai, the Ministry of Navy sent Counselor Ren Guangyu, and Adjutant Zhou Xianzhang. Zhang's entourage included Chief Adjutant Tang Guozhen, Chief Guard Tan Hai, former Director of Foreign Affairs Shen Zutong, Secretary Wu Zhongxian, and Staff Officer He Kui. They sailed on the same ship and stayed at the Deming Hotel, Central Hotel, and Pacific Hotel. Zhang resided at the office. That evening, He Zhuguo, Commander of the 57th Army, and Wei Zonghan, a member of the Pingjin Military Branch, arrived in Hankou from Zhengzhou. Liu Jianxu, Commander of the First Column of the Western Route Army, also came from Hunan. Sun Lianzhong, Commander-in-Chief of the 26th Route Army, Shangguan Yunxiang, Commander-in-Chief of the Fifth Route Army, Pei Changhui, Commander of the 47th Division, and others, who had been waiting in Hankou, successively met with Zhang to ask for instructions. At 10:00 AM on the 26th, after Zhang returned He Chengjun's visit, he immediately accompanied He Zhuguo across the river on the Huasheng small steamer, first going to the Provincial Government to return Zhang Qun's visit and inquire about political measures, and then going to the headquarters to begin work, discussing bandit suppression matters in the three provinces in detail with Chief of Staff Qian Dajun. In the afternoon, he returned to the office across the river. That evening at 7:00 PM, he hosted a banquet for Qian Dajun, He Chengjun, Xu Yuanquan, He Zhuguo, Wei Zonghan, Sun Lianzhong, Shangguan Yunxiang, and various senior generals, during which they discussed military matters related to bandit suppression. Generals from the three provinces will all set out to Hankou to pay their respects, report on defense, and request instructions. After Zhang begins work, he will temporarily work at the Wuchang headquarters and the Hankou office. The swearing-in ceremony is scheduled for the first day of next month, and telegrams have been sent to the Central Government, the National Government, and the Military Affairs Commission, requesting them to send senior officials to Hubei to supervise the oath. After taking office, he will go to Nanchang to meet with Chairman Chiang to request instructions. After returning to Hankou from Nanchang, he will go to the bandit areas of the three provinces for inspection. After that, he will be stationed in the Wuchang headquarters to perform the duties of the Commander-in-Chief and preside over the suppression affairs. As for the political situation in the three provinces, it is said that it will not be changed due to Zhang's arrival in Hankou. There is currently no news of the Northeast Army being transferred south. (26th)

Chairman Chiang Instructs Anhui Province to Eliminate Long-Standing Problems 104

Go Ahead and Act Decisively Based on the Principle of Using Severe Punishments in Times of Chaos.

We Will Vigorously Support You Regardless of Any Difficulties.

Nanchang Correspondence: Liu Zhenhua, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, in order to reform local politics, seeks to eliminate all long-standing problems in the province, and recently submitted the province's political situation and improvement measures to Chairman Chiang for review. After reviewing the report, Chiang believed that Anhui Province's long-standing problems had persisted for a long time, and that the matters mentioned in the report were all crucial plans. Yesterday, he specifically issued instructions to follow the points that should be corrected in the report, and ordered the principle of using severe punishments in times of chaos to be used to eliminate corruption and eradicate local bullies. The original text said, "The report has been reviewed. It has been found that Anhui Province's long-standing problems have persisted for a long time, and that the matters mentioned in the report are all crucial plans. Except for water conservancy and mining, which will be handled separately after funds have been raised, the points that should be corrected in the report are listed as follows. The first section of item A of the report states that the problem with Anhui Province's taxes lies entirely in the registration books, embezzlement of public funds, and reliance on large households as protectors, so we have no choice but to protect large households. If we want to clear up taxes, we must first eliminate the registration books and allow the people to submit them to the treasury themselves, so that we can verify the actual situation. In particular, we should thoroughly investigate those who seek tax exemption in the name of ancestral hall public funds and ensure that they are all included in the regular tax. Otherwise, I am afraid that it will still not be easy to thoroughly rectify the situation. Also, the first section of item B states that Anhui Province's gentry factions are complex, and county magistrates are indecisive, hoping to protect their positions, so that county administration cannot proceed. What you have stated has hit the nail on the head, but the biggest reason why county magistrates do not dare to deal with the situation strictly is that they are afraid of the local bullies inciting unrest. Once local unrest occurs, regardless of right or wrong, if the county magistrate does not handle it well, he will have no excuse. If the provincial authorities do not understand the truth, not only will their positions be questioned, but they will also inevitably suffer future troubles, so they all shirk their responsibilities and live in peace. This matter cannot be blamed solely on the county magistrates. The provincial authorities should carefully select candidates, first have deep confidence in them, and vigorously support them in case of trouble, so that they will not be indecisive. Also, the third section of item B states that everyone knows the problems with corvée labor. If we can clearly stipulate the funds, it will not be difficult to gradually reform the situation, but the amount of funds is not small. What specific funds does the provincial treasury have to prepare for expenditure? If it exists only in name, it is still just a change of soup but not of medicine. The fourth section of item B states that people who accuse officials must provide security and guarantees, which is intended to investigate the truth and prevent false accusations. This matter must be strictly enforced, but we cannot do without measures to crack down on the abuse of telegrams to accuse officials. Also, the various sections of item C list four kinds of malpractices, all of which are true, but the report still does not have any reform measures. That is, the chairman's handling of the strike wave last year was only a temporary response. We must know that student unrest is incited by local bullies. If we can eradicate these local bullies, we will have a clear idea of how to handle the situation. As for bad principals and teachers, their qualifications should be revoked. For a small number of bad students, they should be expelled from school. For all bad students, the school should be closed down. In this way, we can save the declining morals in the slightest degree. Also, the first section of item D states that having roads but no cars is the same as having no roads. The difficulty of car operation is that military and political circles recklessly detain and use them, resulting in cars breaking down and companies losing money, so they will inevitably regard it as a dangerous path. If the province does not pay attention to road operation, I am afraid that it will be difficult for transportation to develop. Also, the final section states that the prohibition of opium is the most important political task of today. The headquarters of the three provinces have repeatedly issued strict prohibitions, divided into three periods, and checked and eradicated on schedule, clearly stipulating the death penalty. We should abide by these brilliant instructions, but the report states that in various counties in northern Anhui, some people are secretly in charge, inciting the planting of opium everywhere since the interregnum, with the intention of inciting unrest and expanding it. Reading this, I cannot help but be horrified. What are the commissioners and county magistrates of the province doing? For such an important political task as the prohibition of opium, which has been reiterated many times, why have they abandoned their duties to this extent? Moreover, there are heavy troops stationed in northern Anhui. How can there be no reason to suppress and sanction them? You should immediately check and eradicate them strictly. If opium seedlings are found when the time comes, we will definitely hold the director of the Civil Affairs Department and the responsible commissioner and county magistrate accountable, and we must not use empty words to perfunctorily deal with the matter. Except for the above-mentioned sections and those that need to be handled separately, the rest should be handled as proposed. The chairman should immediately act decisively based on the principle of using severe punishments in times of chaos, and we will vigorously support you regardless of any difficulties. If we can eliminate corruption and eradicate local bullies, then there is no fear that politics will not be refreshed one day. We have high hopes for this. This order." (February 26)

Baoshan Continues Dredging the Gan River and Malutang 105

Malutang, which runs east-west, is the main trunk river in the Fifth District. It has been in disrepair for many years and is heavily silted. During the winter of the 20th year, when it was being dredged, the project was not even halfway completed when the January 28th Incident suddenly occurred, and it was suspended halfway. More than two years have passed since then, and dredging has not continued. Farmers and businessmen alike have suffered. District Chief Shen Buying, in view of this, planned to continue dredging and submitted it to the county for approval. He appointed District Chief Shen of the Fifth District as the director of the project office, and District Chiefs Yan Guangen and Wang Qingtao of the First and Fourth Districts as deputy directors to be responsible for the implementation. The dam was broken and construction began on January 16th. Now, thanks to the efforts of the director and supervisors, the project is already more than halfway completed, and it is said that it is scheduled to be completed by March 15th to maintain farmland irrigation.

Changshu Administrative Districts Merged and Reduced 109

In recent years, the economy has declined, and various expenses have had to be reduced. The same is true for administrative aspects. On the afternoon of the 26th of this month, the county convened a meeting of district chiefs to reduce expenses and engage in streamlining. It has been decided that the county's original fifteen administrative districts will be reduced by seven. Except for the first and fourth districts, which will remain unchanged, the rest will generally merge two districts into one. As for the funding, it was originally planned to allocate 300 yuan per district per month, but now it has been reduced to 180 yuan. The regions will be re-planned and divided separately.

Fire at Qianwanli Bridge in Suzhou 110

Xu Henggan's family in Qianwanli Bridge shantytown near Suzhou Railway Station, due to carelessness with the lanterns hung for the Lantern Festival on the 13th night of the lunar year, caused a fire. Wang Er'a, an undecided thief and plasterer detained in the Wuxian County Local Court Detention Center, took advantage of the carelessness of the guards at 1:20 PM yesterday (27th) to jump up, climb onto the roof rafters, and tear off the roof. Wuxi Epidemic Diseases Rampant 112

Recently, the weather has been unseasonably cold and warm, with intermittent rain and sunshine, causing an epidemic. Among those suffering from epidemic diseases this week, mumps is the most prevalent, followed by whooping cough, diphtheria, and then scarlet fever, meningitis, and smallpox. Post and Telecommunications Bureaus Merged 113

Zhu Jiaqi, Minister of Communications, recently stated that the post and telegraph bureaus in various counties are both transportation businesses, but they have traditionally been independent of each other, not only lacking coordination in business but also wasting expenses. Therefore, he plans to merge the post and telegraph bureaus in various counties. The local telegraph bureau has received a clear order from the Ministry of Communications. According to the person in charge of the bureau, after the post and telegraph bureaus are merged, all post office branches will have telegraph receiving and sending offices. People can send telegrams at various post office branches without having to go to the telegraph bureau. Moreover, in various European and Western countries, the post and telegraph bureaus are combined into one. It is also heard that the merger will start with the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hubei, but Shanghai and other places will be temporarily postponed due to the difficulty of merging.

Changzhou and Liang County Rice and Bean Industry Increase Commission Dispute 114

The rice and bean industry associations of Wujin and Wuxi counties decided to change the original commission of 99 for a string of cash to 98.4, effective from the 18th of this month, due to the drastic drop in grain prices and insufficient expenses. The two counties' associations jointly published a notice in the newspaper announcing the implementation beforehand. However, the Bengbu Grain Merchant Association and the Jiangsu Bengbu Grain Merchant Association and other groups believed that the private addition of commissions was exploiting the grain merchants, so they jointly submitted a request to the Department of Construction and the governments of Wujin and Wuxi counties, requesting the factory to add a ban to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Yesterday (26th), the County Government also received an order from the Department of Construction, roughly stating what the actual situation was and whether a ban should be imposed. It ordered a joint investigation and verification with the Wuxi County Government in accordance with the local commercial and economic situation and to report the investigation for consideration. In addition, representatives of the rice and bean industries in the two counties recently held a meeting and decided that, according to Bengbu's precedent, miscellaneous grains with a price of less than ten yuan per dan would have a commission of one jiao deducted, and those with a price of more than ten yuan per dan would still be calculated according to 99 for a string of cash.

Jiaxing Yuxian Robbery Case Provincial Order Strict Arrest 115

Shen Baocheng's Nanhua store in Yuxian Town, Jiaxing, was robbed at about 9:00 PM on February 3rd, and more than 300 yuan in silver dollars were stolen. A report was made to request the arrest of the stolen goods. At the same time, he should still urge his subordinates to strictly arrest and hand over the suspects for investigation without delay.

Hangzhou Wang Hanlun Divorce Officially Filed 120

Wang Hanlun, a veteran star in the Shanghai film industry, remarried Wang Jihuan, a famous local gentry in western Zhejiang's Changxing, last August. After living together for seven months, their relationship broke down. Wang then lived separately at No. 10 Zijinguang Lane with the old lady. She filed a request with the Hangzhou Local Court Mediation Office, asking Wang Jihuan to pay more than 520,000 yuan in alimony and damages. After a court mediation, Wang Jihuan did not arrive, and the mediation failed. Both parties decided to meet in court and were unwilling to make any concessions. Wang Hanlun has now prepared to pay the litigation fee of 2,500 yuan and entrusted lawyer Zhang Tao to officially file a lawsuit with the court.

Special Mention

An Impressionistic Account of an Economic Survey in Guangxi Province (4): Qian Jiaxun 121

For more than a month afterwards, besides attending several banquets hosted by the provincial authorities, we devoted all our time to the study of existing economic data on Guangxi. We meticulously reviewed all kinds of publications published by various Guangxi institutions, newspapers, magazines, and the materials for the Guangxi Yearbook that the Statistics Bureau was compiling. We called this period the preparatory period for the survey. Before describing our impressions of the survey in detail, I will take this opportunity to first talk about the civil defense corps and highways in Guangxi.

The civil defense corps is one of the major policies to which the Guangxi authorities are devoting all their efforts. The provincial authorities have two slogans: "Embed soldiers in the corps, embed generals in schools." Regardless of whether this policy is right or wrong, we believe that their courage and spirit are worthy of deep attention from the people of the country. What does it mean to "embed soldiers in the corps"? This means militarizing the civil defense corps and civilianizing the military. Currently, all the civil defense corps in Guangxi Province are under the command of the provincial government chairman. They divided the civil defense corps of the entire province into six districts according to the old dao circuits (previously divided into twelve districts). Each district has one commander and one deputy commander. Below the district is the county, and each county has one commander and one deputy commander. The county magistrate concurrently serves as the commander, and the deputy commander is appointed by the provincial government. Below the county are the standing force, the reserve force, and the auxiliary force. The standing force is discharged every six months, twice a year. After discharge, they become the reserve force. The entire province has a total of two hundred and fifty-one standing force teams, each with ninety people. Each year, at least 40,000 able-bodied men receive military training. Regardless of their occupation (except for public officials and teachers), all members of the reserve force and auxiliary force, aged twenty to forty, are incorporated into the auxiliary force and perform civil defense duties. The reserve force and auxiliary force conduct large-scale autumn exercises during the slack farming season in autumn and winter. In addition, they select dates for further training. According to this method, it is estimated that 280,000 people can be trained in the auxiliary force each year, 40,000 in the standing force, for a total of 320,000 people. Within three years, one million able-bodied men can be trained. Assuming that the total population of Guangxi is 12 million, of which 6 million are women and 3 million are elderly, young, and disabled, there are still 3 million able-bodied men. If this plan is implemented step by step, within ten years, all able-bodied men in Guangxi will become elite soldiers. But now that there are soldiers, where will the officers come from? Therefore, they proposed the plan of "embedding generals in schools," that is, the training of civil defense corps officers. Military training is implemented in schools above the senior high school level in the province. Graduates can become civil defense corps team leaders or platoon leaders. Guangxi has four senior high schools and one university. All graduates are transferred to fill civil defense corps officers, which is sufficient for distribution. According to them, this method is good for the civil defense corps. For the students themselves, they will not be unemployed after graduation and become high-level idlers. They can handle civil defense corps and local self-government affairs. This is the training of lower-level cadres in the civil defense corps, which refers to peacetime. As for wartime, that is, during general mobilization, when a large number of cadres are needed, they can also be transferred from the civil defense corps cadre training center and graduates of schools above senior high school. From this point of view, after three years, the entire province will have one million able-bodied men who have received military training, and the lower-level cadres will also have a place to settle down. This is very noteworthy. As for the funding for the civil defense corps, in the past, the expenses of the headquarters and district headquarters were provided by the provincial treasury. The expenses of the county civil defense corps headquarters and the salaries of the standing force were raised locally by each county. Later, because this method was not only close to harshness but also led to embezzlement and corruption, from the 21st year, all expenses of civil defense corps organizations at the provincial, district, and county levels, as well as special service teams, standing forces, reserve forces, and various teams, were uniformly provided by the provincial treasury. The civil defense corps' firearms are also purchased by the government.

Regarding military training in schools, the Guangxi Provincial Government passed a regulation in May of the 21st year. All senior high school students must receive 1,200 hours of military training during their study period. In the first four semesters, the emphasis is on technical training. In the last two semesters, they specialize in academic courses. During the summer vacation of each year, they also conduct very strict field exercises for two weeks. The military academic subjects in the early stage are set at three credits per semester, and the later stage is set at one credit per semester. Military discipline is calculated according to conduct scores. Those who do not have enough military training credits or fail in military discipline are not allowed to graduate or advance to a higher school. Military training in various middle schools and Guangxi University is extremely strict. In addition to receiving military training, students must also enforce military discipline in the school. Mr. Bai Jiansheng said in a speech to students in Nanning, "High school students should not only actively train in military academic subjects, but also manage all students' actions with military management methods to make students' lives militarized and disciplined." However, because of the excessive emphasis on military management, abuses sometimes inevitably occur. A colleague at Guangxi University told me that last year, a military instructor at the school arrested two students and put them in jail, which caused a storm. The Nanning Republic Daily once published that a student at a certain school was expelled because he went to eat before mealtime. The last two sentences of the notice were, "Immediately expel the student from school to maintain military discipline and school spirit." Putting "military discipline" before "school spirit" shows their educational spirit. After the implementation of military training, it initially aroused opposition from students in various schools. Later, the authorities stated, "Guangxi is training the civil defense corps for national defense and conducting military training to train officers for foreign wars. If one person opposes, one person will be expelled. If the whole school opposes, the whole school will be disbanded." Later, more than 20 student representatives of Guangxi University were expelled, and this storm subsided. However, according to the authorities of various schools, the number of students who voluntarily withdrew from school due to military training is not small, and some have exceeded one-quarter. It is said that now even voluntary withdrawal is prohibited (a certain authority stated that even voluntary withdrawal must be investigated for family members). The number of withdrawals should be reduced. We are laymen in politics and do not want to elaborate on the advantages and disadvantages of this kind of military national education.

Next, let's discuss highways. Highways are the most obvious achievement in Guangxi's construction. Because Guangxi has not built railways until recently, transportation relies entirely on waterways. There are three main rivers in Guangxi: the Yong River, the Tan River, and the Liu River. Wuzhou is located in the lower reaches of the West River. All passengers and goods coming from the Yong, Liu, and Tan Rivers, that is, all passengers and goods from the entire Guangxi and parts of Yunnan and Guizhou, enter and exit through Wuzhou. Therefore, Wuzhou actually holds the transportation hub of the entire province. Although other ports such as Gui, Liu, Yong, Long, and Se all have waterways that can be used, every time during the transition between spring and winter, there are many shoals and the water is dry, and transportation is extremely difficult. Sometimes, ships have to go into the water to carry and lift them to overcome them. However, travel also takes ten days. Since the active construction of highways in recent years, as of recently, a total of 7,294 li of highways have been completed. The completed trunk lines are listed below:

Yongliu Road: Nanning to Liuzhou, 675 li

Liugui Road: Liuzhou to Guilin, 540 li

Guiquanh Road: Guilin to Quanzhou, 320 li

Guiyong Road: Guilin to Yongfu, 110 li

Lihe Road: Lipu to He County, 425 li

Dachi Road: Datang to Hechi, 430 li

Liuwu Road: Liuzhou to Wuxuan, 240 li

Liuchang Road: Liuzhou to Chang'an, 300 li

Bingui Road: Binyang to Gui County, 200 li

Bingshang Road: Binyang to Shanglin, 100 li

Yongwu Road: Nanning to Wuming, 120 li

Yonglong Road: Nanning to Longzhou, 640 li

Guiyu Road: Gui County to Yulin, 205 li

Yubo Road: Yulin to Bobai, 141 li

Yulu Road: Yulin to Shijiao, 220 li

Rongyu Road: Rong County to Yulin, 190 li

Rongcang Road: Rong County to Wuzhou, 200 li

Baiping Road: Baise to Pingma, 170 li

Danchi Road: Nandan to Hechi, 280 li

Yongyu Road: Nanning to Yulin, 235 li

(Other branch lines and county roads less than 100 li are not recorded)

The total length of trunk lines and branch lines reaches more than 7,200 li, which is indeed a great convenience for travelers. Since the completion of the highways, the journey that used to take 20 days can now be reached within two or three days. Taking Wuzhou and Longzhou, which are connected by navigable routes, as an example, it used to take three or four days to go from Wuzhou to Nanning by waterway, and another seven or eight days from Nanning to Longzhou, totaling more than ten days. Now, it takes one day from Wuzhou to Nanning, and one day from Nanning to Longzhou. In other words, it only takes two days from the easternmost part of the province to the southwesternmost part.

Rumors in Banking Circles About the Government's Attitude Towards the Silver Agreement 132

If it is approved, then speculators will transport silver out on a large scale. At the same time, foreign goods are imported, and our country lacks the ability to exchange goods. For example, soybeans, a large commodity produced in the Northeast, have been seized by the puppet Manchukuo, and the silk in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has suffered a setback. Although our government has not temporarily approved the silver agreement for a while, but it is delayed until a considerable time, and I am afraid that it will not be possible to not approve it after all.

Economic Expert Xu Peikun Discusses the U.S. Raising Silver Prices 133

After the United States implemented a policy of raising gold prices, it has recently proposed raising silver prices again, attracting worldwide attention. Our country, as a silver-using nation, will naturally be affected in many ways, and we should prepare countermeasures in a timely manner. However, the changes in silver prices and their relationship to our country's economy are extremely complex. A simple analysis cannot fully reveal the underlying meaning, nor can it be clearly explained by using a few foreign terms. Moreover, President Roosevelt's implementation of gold and silver policies to cope with the extremely panicked global economic environment is an immortal achievement, benefiting both the world and people's hearts, and making great contributions to the welfare of the people. We should sincerely and carefully study the cause and effect of his policies, as well as our country's response, so that in the midst of the surging economic tide, our country may be able to save itself from its predicament. To explain the relationship between raising silver prices and our country's interests, we must first understand the following points:

(1) The Reasons for Low Commodity Prices in Our Country The causes of commodity price fluctuations are extremely complex. Some are caused by the expansion and contraction of the money supply, some by cost factors, and others by supply and demand. There are many conflicting theories, making it difficult to determine what is correct. However, the expansion and contraction of the money supply, to some extent, is related to commodity prices, hence the quantity theory of money. However, it would be a grave error to assert that the expansion and contraction of the money supply has a direct proportional relationship with commodity price fluctuations, and to hastily regard the amount of money as the sole cause of commodity price fluctuations. Commodity price changes depend on the times, environment, and factors. Sometimes there is only one cause of change, and sometimes there are several. Experts in various countries have discussed this in detail, so there is no need to elaborate here. Examining the prices of various commodities in our country in recent years, they have been declining step by step. Although there are multiple reasons for this, the relationship with the money supply is extremely minimal and not worth mentioning. Taking the silk industry as an example, foreign markets have long been seized by Japan and other countries, while the domestic market has suffered a double blow. First, the people are suffering from the pressure of economic depression, and their purchasing power is extremely weak. Second, the invasion of artificial silk from various countries is very popular among the people, and its promotion is extensive and far-reaching, leading to the gradual decline of our country's inherent silk industry and the fall in silk prices. As for the tea industry, foreign markets have long been taken away by India, Ceylon, and other countries. Our country's black tea has been abandoned, and green tea sales are better, but due to its low quality and sluggish sales, our country's black tea has plummeted. As for the cotton industry, in recent years, yarn prices have continued to fall, and the reason is entirely due to natural disasters and man-made disasters. The Northeast market has been seized, while the price of cotton has slightly increased, which is due to the insufficient domestic cotton supply, not the amount of money. As for rice, wheat, flour, and miscellaneous grains, their prices have all fallen uniformly, and the reason is entirely due to the dumping of foreign grains in our country's market. To sum up the above-mentioned commodity prices, the cause of their changes is definitely not the money supply. Now let's cite an example to prove the contrary. In recent years, the amount of silver flowing into Shanghai from all over the country has been increasing day by day. In January of the 20th year of the Republic of China, it was 275,573,000 yuan (converted into silver dollars), and in December of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, it was 508,230,000 yuan, an increase of almost onefold. Why is it that other commodity prices have fallen, except for rent, which has increased? The reason for the increase in rent also has special reasons, which will not be discussed for the time being. From this, it can be seen that the amount of money has little causal relationship with commodity prices in our country.

(2) The Reasons for the Formation of International Trade To put it simply, goods from countries with low commodity prices can definitely be imported into countries with higher commodity prices for sale, and the cash of the importing country must flow out, and commodity prices will fall accordingly. The situation in the exporting country is the opposite. Cash inflows cause commodity prices to gradually rise. Items that could be sold abroad cheaply in the past are now being imported from other countries cheaply. What was previously a trade surplus is now a trade deficit, and gold must flow out again. It flows continuously and follows its course. However, this situation does not exist in our country. Suppose, as some people worry, that after the price of silver increases, the commodity prices in our country will have to fall. Then it is impossible for expensive foreign goods to be imported into countries with low commodity prices, and cheap goods from our country can be imported into countries with high commodity prices. What do we have to fear? Suppose again that if the price of silver increases and the prices of goods are suppressed, our cheap goods still cannot be exported. Then can we increase the export of expensive goods when the price of silver falls and the prices of goods rise? When gold was expensive and silver was cheap the year before last, commodity prices also fell. People thought that exports would definitely increase greatly, but the result was greatly disappointing. Those who care about current affairs can still remember this. In short, our country's international trade is not absolutely based on changes in the price of silver, but on whether Chinese and foreign merchants can make a profit. Our country's domestic market has become fragmented due to internal turmoil and external troubles. Our country's industry and commerce depend entirely on the promotion of international trade to boost it. This is what we should consider carefully when discussing the price of silver.

(3) The Problem of Silver Outflow If the United States implements a policy of raising the price of silver and absorbs silver in the Chinese market, then the outflow of silver will inevitably become a problem, without any doubt. However, this problem is not difficult to deal with, and there is no need to panic. Recall that in May of last year, the price of silver in New York was 15% higher than the price of silver in Shanghai. How much silver flowed out at that time? Even if foreign goods are dumped in our country's market, silver must flow out. Since our country has always been a country with a trade deficit, silver must flow out (unless our country stops all trade with other countries). But at the same time, we must pay attention to the expenses of foreign government officials, travelers, missionaries, etc. in China, and all investment funds remitted by overseas Chinese to China must be paid in silver. Therefore, the silver that flows out will still flow back. Moreover, the United States will definitely not rashly raise the price of silver and immediately absorb and transport it away. When it is necessary to preserve silver, it can be dealt with. If we advocate prohibiting the export of silver and levying export taxes on silver at this time, it will cause panic, shake credit, and affect the public debt market. Therefore, it is better to remain calm and let things take their course.

(4) The Problem of Gold and Silver Standards Our country is on the silver standard, while the United States is on the gold standard. Our positions are different. The United States is a silver-producing country, while our country is not. Therefore, when the price of silver rises, silver producers can obtain huge profits, while non-silver producers have no benefit. Therefore, the interests conflict. Why should we advocate raising the price of silver to benefit others? This argument is not without reason. However, this point is actually self-defeating. If our country does not want to raise the price of silver, the opposite is to raise the price of gold. How can raising the price of gold not benefit others? How can our country transform from a non-gold-producing country to a gold-producing country in an instant? Our country is neither a gold-producing country nor a silver-producing country (we may be able to mine large amounts of gold and silver in the future). Therefore, the rise and fall of gold and silver prices is a problem. Our country's only goal is to seek an appropriate method to stabilize the prices of gold and silver, so that we are not affected by the drastic changes in these prices. It is not like England, which has gold mines, or the United States, which has silver mines, where there are conflicts of interest. When the price of gold soared the year before last, our country was fortunate to adopt the silver standard and was not swept into the vortex of the collapse of the gold standard. Now that the price of silver is gradually rising, we can make good use of the opportunity and use this huge amount of silver value. The government may impose strict supervision on imported goods and prohibit the import of various unnecessary consumer goods, so as to avoid unnecessary increases in trade deficits. When the price of silver rises to a considerable level, a stable and appropriate ratio can be established with the price of gold, and countries can adopt the same monetary system. After that, trade between countries will never be affected by the ratio of gold to silver. The smokescreen of currency is gone, and in the future, international trade will depend entirely on the commodity prices and production costs of each country as tools for competition. In fact, the effect of the currency smokescreen in China is extremely minimal, as mentioned above.

(5) The Impact of Our Country's Tariffs If the price of silver rises, tariff revenue, converted into silver dollars based on customs gold, will inevitably decrease. Assuming that one customs gold unit could be exchanged for two silver dollars in the past, now that the price of silver is high, it can only be exchanged for one and a half or one silver dollar. The loss will naturally be considerable. Although this conversion loss is unavoidable, we can also predict that the quantity and value of import and export trade can increase, and the total revenue of the customs can definitely increase. The result after conversion can also increase. Currently, due to the slight increase in the price of silver, the silk market has shown signs of activity, and transactions have gradually begun. The export goods from North China to the United States in January of this year increased by about 70% compared with the same month last year. The advantages and disadvantages of raising the price of silver can also be seen from this.

In summary, when we study the issue of silver prices, we must adopt scientific methods, stand in the position of a third party, and seek the welfare of the public. I respectfully offer my humble opinions as an ordinary citizen, and I hope that readers will correct me.

News of the Memorial Service for Wu Chaoshu 134

Today's Inaugural Meeting

People from all walks of life, institutions, and organizations across the country, as well as individuals, are planning to hold a memorial service in Shanghai for the late Wu Chaoshu, a member of the National Government who was highly respected both at home and abroad. Representatives from all parties will gather together to discuss the memorial arrangements. The future ceremony will be extremely solemn and mournful.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Sanctions for Non-Membership in Guilds 136

The Prerequisite for Implementing Economic Control

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industry, stating that in August of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, affiliated guilds, including the Sausage Industry Guild, the Chinese and Foreign Grocery Industry Guild, and the Cosmetics Industry Guild, jointly stated that all members of the same industry should join the guild, and the legislative body had established clear provisions. The current issue to be discussed is how the administrative body should implement this. Therefore, the affiliated guild submitted a request to the Executive Yuan on the 31st of that month, requesting that the Executive Yuan stipulate sanctions for non-membership in guilds. If this matter has no implementation method, then Article 7 of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds, even though it changed the word "may" to "shall" in the phrase "Companies and firms in the same industry shall be members of the same industry guild," companies and firms would turn a blind eye, and the law would still be a dead letter. Therefore, there must be an implementation method to implement the spirit of the amendment to that article. Moreover, supplementing the implementation method is based on the authorization of Article 7 of the Guild Law, which is the authority of the administrative body, not the legislative body. Therefore, at that time, it was not submitted to the Legislative Yuan separately for this reason. Later, on September 12th of the same year, a letter was received from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, which stated that the President had instructed that the matters presented should be submitted to the Ministry of Industry for review. The letter was copied and sent for reference. After that, how the Ministry of Industry decided was not known. Earlier, in June of the 22nd year, more than 90 guilds, including the Sausage Industry Guild, stated that those in the same industry who resisted joining the guild should be punished as resisting national administrative power, and forced to join the guild. The affiliated guild submitted a request to the Bureau of Social Affairs to submit it for review. On December 27th of last year, the Bureau issued an order through the Municipal Government to the Ministry of Industry, No. 21883, stating that this matter had been forwarded to the Executive Yuan to consult with the Legislative Yuan for relief. Later, an order was received from the Yuan, approving the Legislative Yuan's reply, stating that the case had been ordered to be jointly discussed by the Economic and Commercial Law Committees of the Yuan. The members of the committees believed that companies and firms in the same industry should join the guild. The seventh article of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds had been amended to state that companies and firms in the same industry shall be members of the same industry guild, and it was promulgated by the National Government on September 15th of the 21st year. There is no need to amend other articles at this time. The intention of the Legislative Yuan seems to be that the implementation method regarding membership does not need to go through the legislative process again. Therefore, it resolutely decided that there is no need to amend other articles again. Moreover, the Ministry of Industry further stated at the end of the consultation that "there is no need to discuss the matter of resisting membership" as the conclusion of the case. As for how to deal with those who should join the guild but resist joining, the Legislative Yuan believes that there is no need to amend it again through the legislative process, and the competent ministry has not issued an order to implement the law based on its authority. The effect of the clause in Article 7 of the Guild Law that all members of the same industry should join the guild is equivalent to being completely eliminated. If the ministries believe that compulsory membership is not necessary, then if there are already seven or more members in the same industry, there is no need to force them to organize a guild according to the law, and Article 7 of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds should not have been amended from "may be members of the same industry guild" to "shall be members of the same industry guild." Now, one party believes that there is a need for compulsory membership, while the other party believes that there is no need to discuss the matter of resisting membership. The legislative intent is obviously inconsistent. In the past two years, the number of trade deficits has been the largest in our country's trade history. The theories of production control and economic control have been very popular for a while, wanting to rely on this as a remedy. With the vastness of our country's territory and the inability to concentrate administrative power, it is impossible to imitate Europe and the United States and implement control overnight. We rely on each industry itself to have a strong and powerful organization, each implementing individual control within its scope of business, so that it can be a solid barrier to resist the rising tide of economic invasion. Therefore, the tasks undertaken by industrial and commercial organizations today are different from those of the past, and the legislative intent should also change with the times. Moreover, what is being requested now is not the issue of compulsory membership, but how to implement the compulsory membership permitted by law. This matter has been discussed for years, but there has been no result. Many of the guilds under the affiliated guild have been virtually suspended because of this. The life of a guild depends on its members. Those who have not joined cannot be forced to come, and those who have already joined gradually leave due to the heavy burden of obligations. How can it be expected that it will not avoid collapsing? In this situation, how can it be expected to fulfill its mission and share a part of the task of controlling the economy? Therefore, the repeated reminders of the affiliated guild are not for the survival of the guild, but for the rise and fall of the national economy. Therefore, without fear of being presumptuous, we reiterate the previous request, hoping that your Yuan will consider and approve it, and properly stipulate an appropriate implementation method for companies and firms in the same industry that should join the guild but consistently refuse to join, so that there is something to follow. This is really for the public benefit.

The Fujian Relief Association Requests Government Relief for Overseas Chinese 138

The Fujian Western Overseas Group Relief Association, feeling that the overseas Chinese crisis is imminent, telegraphed the government yesterday to seek relief. The telegram is recorded as follows: Chairman Chen of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee of the Nanjing National Government. We, the overseas Chinese, are scattered in various countries around the world. In the past, the number reached more than 20 million. However, in recent years, due to extreme oppression by local governments, no less than millions have fled to foreign lands and returned to the country in a state of distress. In addition, the Dutch government has promulgated harsh regulations, Mexico has been fiercely anti-Chinese, and the massacre of overseas Chinese by the Siamese government last year was even more tragic. Most of our overseas Chinese are engaged in industry and commerce, and the economic power of various places over the years has been in the hands of the Chinese. In recent years, due to extreme abuse by local governments and the impact of the global recession, overseas Chinese have no place to stand. They cannot stay, and they cannot return. Those who have returned to the country are suffering because their hometowns are in chaos. At this time, when the overseas Chinese crisis is imminent, we hereby telegraph to earnestly request your association to actively find ways to settle overseas Chinese and provide relief to returning overseas Chinese. As for the massacre of our overseas Chinese by the Siamese government, which is outrageous and extremely illegal, we earnestly request that the government appeal for a strict settlement and conduct a thorough investigation to maintain the national honor and comfort the feelings of the overseas Chinese. The telegram is urgent and awaits orders. The Fujian Western Overseas Group Relief Association kowtows.

Dagong News reports that the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions telegraphed the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the Mass Movement Guidance Committee, and the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating that regarding the selection of labor representatives for this year's International Labor Conference, the union had suggested that labor circles in various places should independently elect one to three comrades with experience, and then the central government should make the final decision, in order to comply with the organizational regulations of the conference, and to consult the public opinion of the national labor circles. The Ministry (Committee) sent personnel to reply, stating that the representatives for this year would be selected from labor circles who have experience, knowledge, and sound physiques. The standards for the candidates proposed by the union have been adopted. However, it has recently been rumored that a certain Central Committee member has been recommended to attend as the labor representative. Upon hearing this, we were extremely surprised. Although this news has not been confirmed, there must be a reason for it. Since the interests of labor are involved, the union is more concerned. Therefore, we specially telegraphed to inquire about the truth. If it is true, we should request an immediate withdrawal and reconsider it in order to live up to the expectations of the labor circles. Otherwise, in order to implement its proposals, the union will unite with labor circles in various places and directly telegraph Geneva to deny it. This is to inform you, hoping you will consider and approve it. The Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions kowtows.

Reorganization Plan for the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau 140

Since Wu Baofeng took over as the director of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, he has been working diligently to reorganize it. He has now drafted various reorganization plans and submitted them to the Ministry of Communications for approval, after which they will be implemented. The reorganization content discussed by Wu is recorded as follows:

Striving for Commercialization 141

Wu first stated that wired telegraphs are affected by the establishment of long-distance telephones and wireless telegraphs. However, the imperfect internal layout of the bureau is also a major reason for the impact on business. Therefore, I will adhere to the principles of commercialization and rationalization in the future and gradually seek reform. The style of the existing buildings and the internal layout all affect business. Although we are limited by funds and cannot completely reform it, we should at least make the building layout like a store and strive for business convenience. Telegraph businesses in European and Western countries are mostly run by merchants. Although China is state-owned now, it cannot be regarded as a government office. We should still adhere to the spirit of business and strive for commercialization.

Cooperation between Wired and Wireless 142

Wu further stated that the Ministry of Communications is planning to merge the operation of wireless telegraphs and wired telegraphs. Most European and Western countries adopt this method. Although this cannot be realized in a short period of time, wired and wireless telegraphs each have their own strengths. We should adhere to the spirit of mutual cooperation and avoid each going its own way. Wired telegraphs may not be as effective as wireless telegraphs in terms of business methods. However, this can only be improved by improving business methods and striving for speed and convenience, which can also be easily remedied. Therefore, I will ensure that the service personnel in the bureau not only make it convenient for the message recipients, but also strive for speed when sending messages. All of this is what I expect to be realized in a short period of time.

Announcement by the Hydrographic Office of the Navy to Bombard Reefs in the Pearl River 143

Notice to Navigating Vessels to Pay Attention

The Hydrographic Office of the Navy issued an announcement that the reefs and rocks in the Pearl River Estuary in Guangdong, due to obstructing navigation, are now being bombarded by the Guangdong Customs. The location is at 113 degrees 15 minutes east longitude and 23 degrees 14 minutes north latitude. During the bombardment of the reefs, a special announcement is issued to inform all ships that when passing through the area during navigation, they should pay special attention to prevent accidents.

The Ministry of Communications Extends the Deadline for Ship Inspection to the End of June 144

Stopping Operation if Inspection is Not Requested within the Deadline

The Ministry of Communications previously stated that Chinese and foreign sailing ships have been old and dilapidated for a long time. Sailing in the outer rivers, they are prone to collapse in the event of wind and waves, which endangers the safety of passengers. Therefore, it specially instructed various shipping companies to have the ships inspected by personnel sent by the Ministry. If the ships are too old or internally decayed, they will be ordered to stop operating to ensure the safety of passengers. At present, shipping companies are enthusiastically applying for inspection. However, there are also not a few ships sailing in remote areas that have not applied for inspection. The deadline for the ship inspection was originally set at the end of December of the 22nd year. Later, to facilitate the inspection of ships from remote areas, it was specially extended by half a year, with the end of June of this year as the deadline. If the inspection is not requested according to the law after the deadline, their operating licenses will be stopped.

Disputes Arise among Workers at the China Merchants Huazhan Wharf 145

Feng Xingcai and other workers at the China Merchants Huazhan Wharf in Pudong initiated the organization of a workers' savings mutual aid association, practicing self-management. In May of last year, it was approved and registered by the Party and government organs and the wharf business office. Since its establishment, there have been no disputes. Unexpectedly, someone is not allowing the workers to work, is restoring the foreman system, and is using gangsters to cause trouble. It is said that the association will petition the Municipal Party Department, the Bureau of Social Affairs, and the Wharf Business Office in the near future, requesting the abolition of the commission foreman, and punishing the troublemakers who have been bought by the capitalists. It is not known how the Party and government organs of this city will resolve this dispute.

The China International Famine Relief Commission, feeling that the Yellow River flood has caused severe disasters in the provinces of Hebei, Henan, and Shandong, with no less than 3 million victims, has launched a fundraising campaign in major cities across the country to raise funds for agricultural relief for the Yellow River disaster. Fundraising in Shanghai is being conducted by the commission's Shanghai office at 49 Nanjing Road. The donations received have been successively remitted to Beiping and then to the disaster areas. It is heard that the commission has achieved good results in providing agricultural relief loans in Heze, Shandong, and has lent out about 20,000 yuan. The work has been promoted to Dongming County. The donations remitted to Beiping from various parties amount to about 80,000 yuan. It is also heard that Mr. Mei Lanfang's charity performances in Beijing raised about 10,000 yuan for relief, and Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission has also agreed to donate 5,000 yuan to promote it.
