Mackenry Lane Water Bill Controversy 148

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports: Mackenry Lane has over one hundred houses, housing four to five hundred tenant families, mostly laborers. Since the Shanghai War, many have lost their jobs. Last August, the landlord forcibly ordered each household to pay a monthly water fee of two yuan. However, the tenants opposed this. After mediation by the court, it was ruled that the landlord's reasons were insufficient and did not comply with the regulations of the water company. The increase in water fees was rejected. Yesterday, the tenants of the lane suddenly received a notice from the Banca di Credito Italiano, demanding payment within a limited time. The notice stated: "To Whom It May Concern: Since last August, when the water company forced the installation of water meters, our water expenses have increased severalfold. We notified each tenant to pay an additional water fee per household, and most tenants have been paying monthly. However, your household and two others have not paid. We hereby warn you to pay the outstanding water fees from August last year to the end of December, totaling ten yuan, within twenty-four hours. If you fail to pay, we will be forced to stop the water supply and request the court to evict you. We sent two Western bank employees on Tuesday, the 20th of this month, to notify you verbally, so you cannot claim you were not informed. In any case, we consider your refusal to pay the monthly two yuan water fee as a regular notice of termination of lease. Therefore, we will rent out your leased property from April 1st onwards." Upon hearing this, the tenants decided to hold a representative meeting within a few days to discuss how to respond.

Tea Merchants See No Progress in Trade with Russia 149

Russians Want Credit, Chinese Merchants Cannot Provide It

The Guowen News Agency reports: Since the resumption of Sino-Russian diplomatic relations, all industries have sought to promote sales to Russia. Regarding tea exports, which traditionally constitute a large part of trade with Russia, this reporter visited tea merchant Chen Yizhou to inquire about the recent situation. According to him, the resumption of Sino-Russian relations has had little impact on tea merchants. Russian tea buyers do not consider the country of origin, only prioritizing low prices and requiring credit. For example, when buying tea from British merchants, they stipulate payment nine months later. When buying tea from Japanese merchants, they stipulate payment one year or eighteen months later. However, when buying from Chinese merchants, they insist on cash payment. Therefore, although Sino-Russian diplomatic relations have been restored, tea trade has not progressed because of the differing credit terms. Last year, the Guohua Bank lent one million silver dollars to the Russian Trade Cooperation Society, which the Russian merchants used to purchase Chinese tea. At that time, tea merchants felt a slight improvement in business. Unfortunately, the loan was too small. If several million more dollars could be lent, the future of tea merchants would be unlimited. Chen also provided approximate figures for tea trade with Russia since 1927, as recorded below:

1927: Approximately over 10 million yuan

1928: Approximately over 12 million yuan

1929: Approximately over 8 million yuan

1930: Approximately over 6 million yuan

1931: Approximately over 5 million yuan

1932: Approximately over 4 million yuan

1933: Approximately over 4 million yuan

The above figures include both Shanghai and Hankou (exports from other minor ports were minimal), and include black tea, green tea, tea dust, etc. The reporter also inquired about future plans for the tea industry. According to Chen, the only reason for the lack of progress in tea trade is the weak capital of Chinese tea merchants, which prevents them from offering credit. He hopes the government can provide loans to Russian merchants, enabling them to purchase as much Chinese tea as possible. In this way, trade with Russia may return to the state it was in 1928.

Carelessness at a Cotton Shop on Avenue Edward VII 150

Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, a cotton shop at No. 384 Avenue Edward VII in the International Settlement caught fire due to carelessness. Cotton and similar materials are highly flammable, so the fire quickly spread through the roof and to neighboring shops at No. 382, a confectionery shop, and No. 386, a fruit shop. Flames soared into the sky, making it impossible to approach. Fortunately, nearby constables spotted the fire and immediately reported it to the Fire Brigade, which dispatched fire engines to extinguish the blaze. However, the fire was raging and difficult to control. Around 9:00 AM, the fire was gradually extinguished. As a result, three buildings were destroyed. At the same time, it was discovered that a 53-year-old woman named Kang Wei, who lived upstairs at No. 384, was missing. Firefighters searched the area and found her body inside the fire scene. She had been burned to death, her body charred beyond recognition, a tragic sight. The relevant police station sent detectives to transport the body to the morgue for examination, while also investigating the cause of the fire for further action.

Oil Workers Riot 151

Police Open Fire, Wounding Three

The Sino-American Petroleum Company's storage facility is located at the Yangshupu Wharf in Pudong. Loading and unloading of oil products at the facility has traditionally been handled by workers from Yangzhou and Shandong. However, competition for work has led to frequent disputes, and resentment has grown over time. Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, as Yangzhou workers were beginning work at the Sino-American Petroleum Company, Shandong workers attempted to intercept business. Yangzhou workers discovered this, leading to a verbal altercation. Other Yangzhou workers arrived to support their side, creating a potentially violent situation. Shandong workers also rallied in response. About two hundred workers from both sides gathered, creating a noisy scene. Unable to reach an agreement, they armed themselves with carrying poles and engaged in a direct brawl. Police officers from the Public Works Bureau learned of the incident and rushed to suppress the riot and mediate between the parties. However, the Yangzhou workers, feeling they were in the right, refused mediation and claimed the police were biased. They created difficulties for the police. During the chaos, a small number of workers shouted and charged toward the police. The police, fearing for their lives, fired warning shots into the air. However, the workers did not disperse and continued to attack with carrying poles. Unable to do otherwise, the police fired live rounds, hitting and knocking down three leading workers. The crowd hesitated to advance further. At the same time, police officers from the Fourth Precinct of the Third District arrived to maintain order. The riot was prevented from escalating. The three wounded workers were all shot in the legs and are not in critical condition. They were transferred by the Fourth Precinct of the Third District to the Sacred Heart Hospital in Puxi for treatment. Further reports will follow regarding the resolution of this case.

Hospital Nurse Commits Suicide After Losing Job 152

Lei Atang, a native of Ningbo, 18 years old, previously worked as a nurse at the Pingmin Obstetrics Hospital on Huade Road and then transferred to the Da Zhonghua Hospital in Xin Hui Le Li on the Fourth Avenue as a medical intern. Lei was exceptionally intelligent and made great progress in various fields. Recently, after clinics, he frequented brothels and often returned late at night, which displeased the hospital director. He was suddenly dismissed a few days ago. Lei was greatly affected by this and lost his place of residence, feeling depressed. The day before yesterday (26th), he checked into room 321 at the Far East Hotel on Xizang Road. In the evening, he made a phone call to a Miss Yuan at the Pingmin Obstetrics Hospital and then went to sleep. At around 11:00 AM yesterday morning, a female called and asked for the guest in room 321, claiming she was calling from San Ma Road. The doorman, after answering the phone, went to knock on the door of the room, but received no answer for a long time. Suspecting something was amiss, he forced the door open and entered. He saw Lei lying stiffly on the bed, having swallowed poison, barely breathing. Realizing the situation, the doorman reported to the front desk, who in turn reported it to the Zhabei Police Station, sending Officer No. 42 to investigate. The Lei was transported to the Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that he ingested too much poison, and his life is in danger.

Minutes of the Shareholders Meeting of the China Realty Company 153

The China Realty Company, an American enterprise, held its eighth annual shareholders meeting on February 27, 1934, at the company's office in Shanghai. Mr. Satterlee, the vice president of the company, presided over the meeting, making the following announcement to the shareholders: "According to the schedule set for today (4:30 PM), a quorum has been reached. I request the company secretary to begin by reading the notice of the annual shareholders meeting." Notice of the Annual Shareholders Meeting of the China Realty Company: This year's annual shareholders meeting of the company will be held at the company's office at 290 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, on Tuesday, February 27, 1934, at 4:30 PM. All shareholders are expected to attend punctually. If a shareholder wishes to appoint a representative due to other matters, please submit the authorization form to the company's office before 5:00 PM on February 26th to be valid. Furthermore, the transfer of the company's shares will be temporarily suspended from February 19th to 27th, according to regulations. This is hereby announced. Andaom, Secretary of the China Realty Company, By order of the Board of Directors. The company's financial statements have already been sent to all of you. If you approve, I will assume they have been read. From the perspective of a real estate company, 1933 was a most difficult year. Money was unusually loose in the market, and property owners could easily obtain financial assistance. Therefore, owners were unwilling to sell below cost, including interest and expenses. At a time of commercial recession, buyers only sought to purchase cheap properties. Shanghai was affected by the global economic downturn, which our company managed to avoid in the first half of 1932. However, it was not spared in the second half. Based on my past experience, I believe Shanghai will soon return to its original state. The item regarding the China Realty Trust Company in the balance sheet has surely caught your attention. This company is a British company registered in Hong Kong, handling the registration of British titles. Regarding the increase of 1,387,389.71 silver dollars in the company's assets, I would like to clarify to all of you that this increase represents properties purchased this year, which the company believes are cheap and can generate substantial profits. The company expects to profit in the future. The 18 million yuan mortgage was successfully negotiated by the company after nearly a year. I believe this mortgage is an unprecedented personal mortgage in Shanghai. Although it was completed in 1933, the funds were only paid after the company's year-end closing, so it was not included in the financial statements. In 1933, the company handled business totaling 40,015,800 silver dollars, more than the 33,413,200 silver dollars in 1932. However, this figure does not include rental income, property management, insurance, trust, and other miscellaneous income. Finally, I would like to inform all of you that the Board of Directors believes shareholders should enjoy reasonable returns on their investment. The company's smooth operation depends on your financial support. If you agree, the Board of Directors proposes to distribute a dividend of 1.40 yuan per share. If calculated in silver dollars, this dividend is slightly higher than 10 percent. Before any resolutions are made, I am willing to answer any questions you may have." Resolution 1: "I propose that all of last year's business reports, financial statements, and the 1933 dividend of 1.40 yuan per share be approved by everyone present. In addition, the remaining balance of 381,351.18 silver dollars be transferred to the next year's surplus account." Rong Shangqian seconded. Passed. Resolution 2: "Mr. Satterlee and Mr. Sattary have voluntarily resigned from their positions as directors, but they are still qualified to be re-elected, so they will remain candidates." Mr. Li Wei proposed, and Mr. Rong Shangqian seconded, that Mr. Satterlee and Mr. Sattary be re-elected as directors for the next term. Passed. Resolution 3: "Mr. Andaom proposed, and Mr. Li Wei seconded, that E. Maurer, accountant, be appointed as the company's auditor for 1934." Passed.

Astrologer's Scare Tactics: Wealthy Widow Duped Out of Three Thousand Gold Pieces 154

Stacks of Banknotes Transformed into Layers of Wastepaper

Fraudulent Enough to Forge Deposit Slips for Collateral

Yang Letian from Wuxi is engaged in astrology and divination. He formerly had a sign posted at the Oriental Hotel on Xizang Road. Whenever wealthy merchants and tycoons went to discuss their fortunes with him, he would cleverly flatter them with flowery language and speak freely, occasionally using threatening words to instill doubt and fear in his listeners. He would then take the opportunity to blackmail them. There are many victims. For example, the manager of a well-known cigarette company was almost tricked out of ten thousand gold pieces but fortunately woke up early, avoiding the loss. Yang's deceptive tactics can be seen from this. However, there are many superstitious people in Shanghai. What Yang cannot do to one person, he can do to another. Recently, there was a major case in Suzhou where a

Wealthy Woman 155

was swindled out of three thousand gold pieces. The woman, named Xu Ruqun, was married to a man named Bao. Not long after, her husband died, and she became a widow, residing at No. 14 Yile Lane, Danshui Road. Although she is now thirty-eight years old, she is very superstitious. She is also wealthy and likes to burn incense to worship Buddha and consult fortune tellers and physiognomists. Her friend Zhu Baozhen had previously consulted Yang. After being flattered by Yang, she believed his skills were magical and encouraged Xu to go to the Oriental Hotel on August 27th of last year to inquire about her fate. After meeting and talking, Yang observed Xu's psychology and noticed her

Exquisite Clothing 156

He suspected she was wealthy and immediately used his usual tricks, saying her upcoming years would be unlucky and her life palace was unfavorable. If she did not perform rituals to avert these disasters, not only would calamities befall her, but her life would be in danger. He made all sorts of frightening claims. Xu fell for his tactics and begged him to find a way to eliminate the bad luck. Yang asked for fifty gold pieces, claiming it was for the cost of dispelling the stars' influence. Xu gave him the full amount. On September 20th, Yang invited Xu to the Oriental Hotel again, saying that her misfortune could not be averted with just fifty gold pieces. She needed to add one hundred and twenty-eight yuan, which he would use to set up an altar in Wuxi to perform rituals. Xu complied and gave him the money. After just ten days, Yang invited her again by phone to go to the Oriental Hotel. He said, "Of the one hundred and twenty-eight yuan you gave me earlier, forty gold pieces were unclean money, which offended the deities. Not only will it not eliminate the disasters, but it will cause more trouble,

Offending Heaven." 157

While he was speaking, he deliberately looked worried. Xu was very frightened when she saw this and begged for help. Yang initially said there was no way to remedy the situation, but then said he would try. He told her to prepare three hundred gold pieces for use. On October 7th, Xu brought the money to the Oriental Hotel again. After Yang took her banknotes, he told her to face the wall. In an instant, he wrapped something in paper and gave it to her to hold. At the same time, he burned yellow paper with cinnabar symbols drawn on it and told her to draw a similar symbol on a piece of paper, burn it, and then take the paper package home and store it. He told her not to open it without being instructed to do so, otherwise her life would be in danger. She respectfully listened to his instructions and took the package home. In reality, the three hundred yuan banknotes were already in

His Possession, 158

He had replaced them with wastepaper inside the package. If Xu had not been frightened by his scare tactics and had opened the package upon returning home, the scam would have been exposed early on, and she would not have continued to lose her wealth. However, her superstition was too deep, and she regarded the paper package as a dangerous object, placing it without daring to touch it. Until December 6th, Yang saw that the victim was not doing anything and figured that nothing had gone wrong. So, he again invited Xu by phone to go to the Yangtze Hotel and intensified the threatening nature of his conversation. He said that if she wanted to receive divine protection, she should add another eight hundred gold pieces. He also induced her by saying that the money would still be kept by her as before, and it could not be used only during the ritual period. In reality, there was no loss at all. Xu still followed his orders. The next day she brought the money. Yang also

Followed Suit, 159

Only replacing the paper package with a cigarette box. However, the relationship between the two had become very close. Yang learned about Xu's wealth and thought that he could not just rely on this method to deceive her. Therefore, he forged a two thousand yuan deposit slip issued by the Lu Zhenda Foreign Goods Store on Robert Street. On January 6th of this year, he summoned Xu to his house at No. 8 Airen Lane, Avenue Petain, to discuss the difficulty of dispelling the stars' influence. When he asked Xu to add another four hundred yuan, he used the deposit slip as collateral for one thousand five hundred yuan. At this time, Xu still deeply believed in him, so she regarded the forged document as genuine, without any hesitation, and gave him the money. In total, from August 27th to that time, Xu had been swindled out of more than three thousand gold pieces. However, she still had not realized it. Recently, she happened to talk about it with her friend Gu Fan, who was not as foolish as her.

Determined It Was A Scam 160

She insisted that Xu open the paper packages and cigarette boxes that she had brought back each time. Xu was still hesitant at first, but after being persuaded by Fan again and again, she opened them one by one. Sure enough, they were all wastepaper. Xu deeply regretted it and went to Yang's house on February 19th to negotiate. Yang, fearing that if it were publicized, this trick would be difficult to use again and that he would be even more guilty, in order to ease Xu's anger, in addition to writing a confession, he also gave her all the rosewood furniture in his apartment and a car number 2998, valued at two thousand yuan, as compensation. However, the next day Xu discovered that the Lu Zhenda's deposit name,

Was Also A Forgery. 161

It was like pouring oil on the fire. Xu then went to the New Gate Police Station to report the incident, requesting an investigation. The day before yesterday, Detective Ruan Yao and Detective Huang Siming arrested Yang Letian. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court, where Judge Zhan Liangce conducted a preliminary hearing. After the police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the case, he requested that the defendant be punished according to Article 363 of the Criminal Code. Xu Ruqun also recounted the process of being repeatedly defrauded. When the defendant Yang Letian was questioned, he admitted to receiving the various amounts of money from Xu, but claimed that he had a special relationship with her and that the money was not obtained through fraud. He also hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to defend him. Judge Zhan, believing that the case still needed investigation, ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled the hearing.

Japanese Fish Actively Dumped 162

Another Three Thousand Dan of Large Yellow Croaker Imported

Central News Agency reports: Since the Japanese fishing vessel "Wanichi Maru" transported the first batch of Japanese fish for import, fishermen in this city have been feeling extremely uneasy. Unexpectedly, just a few days later, another three thousand dan of Japanese large yellow croaker were imported this week. It is said that each dan is priced at only twelve yuan, and most of them are transported to the capital. Only a small portion is sold in the Shiliupu area of this city. The detailed reports obtained from various sources are listed below:

Large Quantities of Yellow Croaker Imported Again 163

The three thousand dan of Japanese fish imported in the most recent week are all large yellow croaker, transported by Japanese merchants. They are unloaded at the Oriental Air Conditioning Company, operated by Japanese in Yangshupu. The fish are caught in the coastal areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Most of them are transported to Nanjing, packed in cardboard boxes with the words "Kyodo Co., Ltd." marked on the outside. In Nanjing, they are repacked in wooden buckets, using the domestic "Qian Feng" brand to masquerade as domestic goods. Relevant parties in this city have repeatedly telegraphed the Anti-Japanese Association in Nanjing for inspection, but due to their rigorous methods, it is difficult to find any flaws. Therefore, the small-scale fish markets run by Chinese will be taken over by them.

South China Sea Fishing Grounds to Be Plundered 164

Moreover, according to Jin Chuxiang, former chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Fish Inspection and Price Stabilization Committee, although the Russian side has allowed a re-bid in the recent fishing area bidding dispute between Japan and Russia, if Japanese merchants fail again, the fishing industry of our country's seven coastal provinces will be completely plundered by the Japanese. The Japanese have already built fish markets in Dalian and other places and will further explore the South China Sea's fish producing areas. He hopes that the fish market organized by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will be established as soon as possible, so that people all over the country can work together to boycott them and save the situation.

Health Bureau Establishes Clinic in the City Center 172

The City Health Bureau's simple clinic in the city center has been prepared and is located within the Health Bureau building. It began providing medical services on the 26th of this month. The clinic's regulations are as follows: (1) City government and affiliated agency employees seeking treatment for common illnesses shall be governed by these regulations. (2) All patients visiting the clinic must first register and be seen in order of registration. (3) Registration hours are from 9:00 AM to 11:30 AM and 1:00 PM to 4:30 PM daily, except for Saturday afternoons, Sundays, and public holidays when the clinic is closed. (4) The clinic's physicians generally do not make house calls, except in cases of emergency. (5) To prevent dangerous situations, no prescriptions will be filled without the signature of a certified physician. (6) Only medications available in the clinic's pharmacy will be dispensed. (7) The dispensing of dressings and medications requires the approval of the relevant department head of the bureau, and the quantities dispensed will be based on the approved amount. (8) The clinic does not stock patent medicines (such as tonics and injections). (9) These regulations are subject to amendment as needed. (10) These regulations shall take effect upon approval by the city government for record-keeping.

Guest Returning from Xi'an Discusses the Establishment of the Xijing Midwifery School 191

The Shaanxi Private Xijing Midwifery School was founded with a donation from Ms. Fu Xuewen, the wife of Provincial Chairman Shao Lizi, who also serves as the school principal. Ms. Fu is currently in Shanghai for medical treatment and to plan for the school's fund. A guest who recently returned from Xi'an mentioned that the school officially opened on February 18th. The following is an excerpt from the speech by Chairman Shao Lizi: It is naturally not easy to promote a matter, especially to handle midwifery education. Judging from the old midwifery methods in the past, the surgery was clumsy and did not pay attention to hygiene, unlike the new methods of today, which, in addition to disinfection, also apply scientific and rational surgery, so that both mothers and newborns can be safe. Our country has not been able to promote this kind of education until now because the conservative ideas are too deep, always thinking that we have our own national civilization, so we do not learn from others' improved new methods. For example, Japan, before the Meiji Restoration, learned our Chinese books. After the Meiji Restoration, they learned the new medical techniques of Europe and the United States. Therefore, Japan's current medical techniques and theoretical aspects are very famous in the world. In our country, midwives are one of the practitioners of medicine, but they cannot improve the old methods of delivery and do not know how to accept new methods. This phenomenon is really inappropriate. Now that the midwifery school has been established, although the time is relatively late, it is hoped that everyone will devote themselves to learning, and it is not too late. In the future, after completing this kind of education, we must contribute to society. In today's semi-civilized society, most people may not believe in what we have learned, but since we have learned this kind of education, it is naturally our permanent occupation. For pregnant women, we must take care of them with all our hearts to avoid harming the lives of both mother and child. Furthermore, the old midwives do not care about people's lives, they only care about money. The trained midwives are very lazy. When delivering babies for others, they often do not perform the surgery carefully and do not disinfect for others. This is contrary to benevolence. I hope that everyone will encourage each other.

Japanese Actively Dumping Rubber Balloons in China 192

Monopolizing the Patent for Over Twenty Years, Seducing Chinese Children

Our Annual Losses Reach 150,000 to 160,000 Yuan

Rubber balloons, children's toys, sell especially well during the New Year. Available in all colors, they fly and dance in the sky. Children play with them for a short while before they are destroyed, as they are extremely fragile toys. Yesterday, it was learned that rubber balloon toys have always been imported by the Japanese. Although they are small items, the annual sales in our country amount to a huge sum of 150,000 to 160,000 yuan, which is also a significant financial drain. The best imported quality balloons cost about 20 cents each, which does not seem to match the purchasing power of Chinese children. For over twenty years, the Japanese have monopolized the patent for these toys. There are many national rubber product factories in Shanghai, but no one has paid attention to this product. It has now been found that the Jin Xing Arts and Crafts Factory in Zhabei is manufacturing and selling these balloons in this city. It has been in operation for half a year and has achieved excellent results, producing about 100 baskets of balloons per day. The trademark is Jin Xing, and it is also a start-up business among national products. It has been found that the raw materials for balloons are raw rubber, zinc oxide, linseed oil, and gasoline, four kinds. When the raw materials are vaporized to a certain extent, countless two- or three-inch-long glass tubes are used. One end of the tube must be large and bulbous. The bulbous end is dipped into the pot and fully coated with the solution. They are then inserted upside down onto nails and stood up to cool. Then the balloon blank is formed. Depending on its tightness, it can be pulled down from the glass tube one by one after solidification without being destroyed. To make it a balloon, it is then inflated with air to make it expand. Then the mouth of the balloon is tied with a thread, and it can be inflated at any time. Each basket sells for about 1.20 yuan.

Xishan Plum Blossom Viewing Tour 193

In order to promote travel and explore scenic spots, the Sichuan Road China Travel Agency organized the Dengwei Plum Blossom Tour. Due to the lack of mountain sedan chairs, the number of tour members was not large and has been filled as of yesterday. However, many ladies who love to travel have enthusiastically requested to participate. In order to provide more widespread service and promote sightseeing, the agency has organized another Xishan Plum Blossom Viewing Tour, scheduled to depart from Shanghai for Wuxi on the morning of March 4th. The tour group will enjoy the plum blossoms to their heart's content. In the afternoon, they will enjoy the scenery of the renowned Huiquan Mountain and Yuantouzhu. They will return to Shanghai that evening. Enjoying plum blossoms and exploring scenic spots, it will be a double win. The tour is limited to fifty members, and the fee is 15 yuan per person. Ladies who love to travel should not miss this opportunity.

Re-examination Still Required for the Case of Shooting a Prostitute 194

On the afternoon of January 4th of this year, Chen Lanfang was entertaining guests at the Juhua Courtyard, No. 2 Hongyun Lane, Rue Wagner, French Concession, in the room of prostitute Lin Juxian on the third floor. At around 9:00 PM, Zhou Hongsheng, a Chinese detective from the Public Concession, took off his loaded handgun because of an urgent need and hid it under the pillow on the bed in the room. When he turned around to go to the toilet behind the bed, his friend Chen Linrong, out of curiosity, took out the gun to play with it, accidentally touching the trigger. The bullet flew out and injured the prostitute Lin Juxian in the abdomen. She died despite medical treatment. The police arrested Chen Linrong and sent him to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. The trial concluded, and Chen Linrong was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for causing death by negligence. Chen, dissatisfied with the judgment, appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. This has been reported previously. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Chief Justice Guo of the High Court, along with Associate Judges Sun and Fan and Prosecutor Zhang, opened the Third Criminal Court for trial. Yao Zhaodi, a lawyer from the police station, appeared in court. Appellant Chen Linrong stated that he did not actually take out the gun to play with it. He was lying on the bed, and when his head was on the pillow, he felt a hard object touching him under the pillow. When he touched it with his hand, the bullet was fired, causing the accident. The officials then summoned the witnesses Hu Bingchen, Qiu Ruqing, Chen Lanfang, and Zhou Hongsheng to testify about the circumstances at that time. They also ordered Zhou Hongsheng to demonstrate how he placed the handgun on the bed. The court ordered the hearing to be adjourned to a later date.

Thieves Hu Amao and Others Sentenced 195

Thieves Hu Amao from Suzhou and Lu Heshang from the local area, together with several accomplices, including Xue Longquan, who has been arrested and sentenced to imprisonment, robbed the Meixing Watch Store at No. 167 Avenue Edward VII on the evening of June 22nd of last year, stealing more than 200 watches. On January 1st of this year, they robbed the Si Huisi Watch Store at No. 297 Avenue Edward VII, selling the watches for money. After the case occurred, detectives Lu Jinbao and Cao Fuchang and Chinese Detective Cheng Yuming of the French police station learned of it and arrested the two thieves, Hu and Lu, confiscating a six-shot automatic pistol and five bullets, and 31 original stolen watches. They were sent to the Second Special District Local Court, and the police station's lawyer filed a public prosecution for robbery. The details of the interrogation have been reported previously. The trial has now concluded. Yesterday was the sentencing date. At 10:00 AM, the police sent Hu and the others to the court, where Judge Wu Fanglian presided over the First Criminal Court. Hu Amao was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for each of the two robbery crimes, with a total of eight years of imprisonment. Lu Heshang was sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment for each of the two robbery crimes, with a total of five years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was final was calculated at two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. The pistol and bullets were confiscated, and the stolen goods were returned to the owners. After the judgment was made, the Chinese and Western detectives of the Xin Zha Police Station of the Public Concession submitted a document, stating that the defendants were involved in the case of the robbery of the Huade Watch Store on Xin Zha Road in the Public Concession and requesting permission to transfer the two defendants to the police station for interrogation. The court granted permission to transfer the two defendants to the police station for interrogation.

The Four Banks Joint Treasury Reserve is jointly established by the Yien Yieh, Kincheng, China & South Sea, and Continental Banks to exclusively handle the issuance of notes by the China & South Sea Bank. According to the treasury's issuance regulations, notes are issued with full reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for at most 40%. Meng Gaohua Department Store of America Presents Exquisite General Catalog. Meng Gaohua is a famous department store in America with substantial capital and its own factories. Dafang Auditorium Offers Free Rental. Dafang Hotel, located on Zhengjia Muqiao Street, is a rising star in Shanghai's modern hotel industry and can rightly be called the newest and largest hotel in the French Concession. After the building was completed, the interior decoration and furnishings took a year to finish. The hotel opened last Spring Festival. Considering the cramped living conditions of Shanghai citizens and the difficulty of holding weddings and celebrations, as well as the exorbitant rental fees for temporary auditoriums, the managers have decided to offer a large auditorium on the fifth floor for public use free of charge. The auditorium can accommodate over twenty tables, is bright and spacious, and luxuriously decorated. It has sunlight on three sides and platforms at both ends. The platforms are twice the size of the auditorium, and above them are high canopies and stages, allowing families celebrating joyous events ample space for maneuvering and entertainment. At ordinary times, it is used for travelers' meals, banquets, and recreation, also free of charge. All 150 guest rooms, including ordinary rooms ranging from 80 cents to two yuan, have hot water heaters and hot and cold water plumbing. Forty-odd rooms have attached bathrooms, divided into four grades, with the cheapest costing only three yuan and forty cents per day and the most expensive costing no more than four yuan per day. However, room 501 on the fifth floor, divided into four rooms, rents for ten yuan and is the only special room. Furthermore, to reward customers, the hotel is giving away exquisite hot water bags starting today (the 28th), regardless of the size of the room booked.

Letters 213

To the Editor, I recently read a news item in your newspaper dated February 26 about a dispute over the French Concession's restrictions on rickshaw licenses. It does not conform to the facts. Regarding the French Concession's recent restrictions on licenses, our association has repeatedly petitioned the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for assistance and has sent representatives to appeal to the French authorities to provide appropriate relief to unlicensed rickshaw operators. All of this is documented and witnessed by the rickshaw operators. Recently, the unlicensed rickshaw operators, after long waiting with great anticipation, on the 24th of this month, dragged about 60 to 70 unlicensed rickshaws to the entrance of the lane where our association is located (namely, Sanminfang) intending to petition the French Concession authorities together. However, due to a dispute over the levy of one yuan per rickshaw, and because some rickshaw owners did not bring the rickshaws they had promised, the group was uneven, and the crowd was noisy and disorderly. The protest ended without results. At that time, no one was publicly elected as the general representative, and no resolution was made to question the association's handling of the matter. It is clear that someone fabricated the news to confuse the public. Correspondingly, we request your newspaper to make a correction. Respectfully addressed to Mr. News Editor, Shen Bao. Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association. Standing Committee Members: Qiu Chunshan, Zhang Huaiyang, Song Yaokun. February 27.

To the Editor, I recently read in the local news column of your newspaper dated February 27 that the Chinese Red Cross Society will hold a re-election and is scheduled to host news reporters tomorrow. This is completely untrue. Our association, under the order of the Ministry of Interior, will begin soliciting members on March 1st for a period of two months. We have specifically scheduled a reception for news reporters on the 28th and will host a banquet for the team leaders on the 2nd. There will be no re-election or communication matters. We respectfully request a correction. Respectfully addressed to the Editorial Department, Shen Bao. Sincerely, Chinese Red Cross Society. February 27, 1934.

Reading and Answering Questions

Where Should We Start When Studying International Issues? (2) 215

Before answering the several questions you have asked, we feel that we should offer a few words about your "life problems."

From your letter, we know that you are a young person with quite a bit of life experience and also possess a spirit of striving in the struggle for survival. What is currently facing you is the threat of unemployment, which makes you feel that "the future is not optimistic," which is understandable. If we look at this terrible phenomenon of unemployment from the perspective of an individual's future, we cannot avoid feeling "sadness from within." However, if we can see that this is a complete social problem, and that the solution to this problem requires the joint efforts of the masses to first eliminate the bad roots that produce unemployment, then you may not only avoid being pessimistic and passively discouraged by the current hunger, but you will instead develop the courage to fight and maintain a positive outlook for the future! Therefore, while we admire your striving spirit, we must further hope that you will take another step forward and first eliminate the gray thoughts in your hesitation, indecision, and timidity!

The following are answers to the several questions you have asked.

First, you ask whether someone in your living situation "should" and "can" study international issues. We can answer definitively: you "should" study and also "can" study. The reason is simple: today's world is no longer the era of our ancestors. Today, the nations of the world have been linked into a system by a kind of economic tie. There is no longer a piece of land on Earth that can escape the control of today's economic relations. Therefore, the lives of people in every corner of the Earth today are inevitably affected by the world. For example, the United States needs Japanese raw silk, Britain imports huge amounts of grain from all over the world, Japan needs Chinese coal and iron, Russian and American oil, and Indian cotton. China imports American Mobil kerosene, Lancashire cotton cloth, German pigments, fertilizer, machinery from various countries, and Japanese daily necessities. At the same time, China also exports tea, silk, tung oil, soybeans, etc. Everyone has already established close economic relations; they are interdependent and have become a global economy. At the same time, because this relationship takes the form of capitalist production relations, all that is seen in the world are blocks of business markets, thousands of factories producing for the market, and many markets and factories linked together to form economic spheres. These economic spheres are what we call nations, and they are all manufacturing, selling, and competing for markets in a state of anarchy, engaging in economic, political, or even cultural (in the narrow sense) "alliance" and "axis" struggles. However, if something goes wrong in one sphere of the world, it will affect the whole, like a chain where if one link comes loose, it will affect the whole. People living in the world today, whether you are British, Japanese, or Chinese, are all, without exception, directly or indirectly affected internationally. You can no longer close the door and escape reality; you are tightly bound by this network of economic relations, not allowing you to dream of living like the mythical emperors of the past.

Speaking of the current situation of the Chinese people, you cannot help but pay attention to what is happening internationally every day; for example, the current American purchase of silver is not just an economic policy of the United States; it will affect the lives and deaths of the Chinese masses. Why? Because the purpose of the United States in raising the price of silver is to encourage foreign dumping. China is a country that uses silver, and undoubtedly, on the surface, it will be found that China's purchasing power is strengthened (it is not a real increase in purchasing power, but American goods are taking the place of Chinese domestic goods). American goods will flood the Chinese market like a flood with this stimulus, and China's only agricultural market will be replaced by American goods. At that time, it will not only cause the outflow of silver, creating a shortage of currency and causing financial chaos, but the biggest disaster is that it will accelerate the bankruptcy of the rural economy. Therefore, although this event happened in the United States, we cannot but care about it.

Also, the recent Austrian issue, the bloodshed before Paris, the autonomy of Mongolia, the independence of Xinjiang, and the encroachment on Xikang in Tibet, etc., have now become international issues, because these not only have a life-and-death relationship with the Chinese masses, but also affect the world government. All this should be noted not only by the government authorities, but also by us ordinary people, so that we can understand what countermeasures today's government authorities are taking to deal with these problems, and whether they are safeguarding the interests of the masses. If not, how should we supervise them and how should we promote the demands of our people and break through the current national crisis?

Therefore, people like you should naturally study international issues. As for whether you "can," that is even less of a question, because as long as you are willing to study, even an illiterate worker can discuss it with others through conversation, let alone someone who already has the tool of writing?

Second, where should we start when studying international issues? How can we develop correct awareness? Given your level, we feel that you should start with research methods. Originally, international issues are a branch of social science, and the research methods are of course the methods of researching social science.

(To be continued)

Minister of Education Wang Replies to the Representatives of Private Middle Schools in Beiping Who Came to Petition 216

Beiping Gathers Senior Transfer Students and New Students

Beiping Social Bureau Details the Reasons Why Prohibition is Necessary

When the Ban Will Be Lifted Will Be Determined After Sending Personnel to Inspect

(Nanjing, 27th) Wu Baojian, the representative of the joint association of private middle schools in Beiping, who went to Beijing to petition, arrived at the Ministry of Education on the 27th to petition. Secretary Zhou Chen presented the intention, and Minister Wang immediately met with Representative Wu. He explained in detail the situation of private middle schools in Beiping recruiting senior transfer students, and requested that the Ministry of Education give special consideration to the senior transfer students that have already been recruited by the schools this time, and find ways to help them. Minister Wang replied in general: (1) According to the middle school regulations, it is stipulated that middle schools can recruit transfer students, but the local educational administrative organs, when reorganizing the schools in their jurisdiction, may prohibit or restrict the recruitment of transfer students and new students when they deem it necessary. This time, the Beiping Social Bureau listed the reasons why it must prohibit the recruitment of senior transfer students to the Ministry, and the Ministry has approved the record. As for when the ban on recruiting senior transfer students in Beiping will be lifted, it will be determined by the Ministry sending personnel to inspect the extent of the educational reorganization in Beiping in the future. (2) As for how to resolve the issue of the transfer students that have already been recruited by the schools this time, it still needs to be handled by the Beiping Social Bureau. Finally, he informed the representative of the handling process of this matter by the Ministry of Education this time, urging the representative to return to Beiping quickly and not delay the operation of the schools.

The Compilation Process of the China Education Yearbook 217

The Ministry of Education has compiled the first China Education Yearbook, which is scheduled to be published in April. The following is a record of the compilation process published by the colleagues involved in the compilation:

Since the rise of education in our country during the late Qing Dynasty, educational historical materials have accumulated and become complex. Recently, yearbooks have been compiled among provinces and cities for the purpose of comprehensive observation, but they are limited by region and scope. A national yearbook for the whole country is still lacking. The former Minister Zhu Gong saw this and, on March 16 last year, instructed the former Compilation and Examination Department to quickly compile an education yearbook. This is how the first China Education Yearbook came to be.

Considering the complexity of the matter and the difficulty of proceeding, on March 23, Director Zhang Xiushan, Director Guo Xinsong, Director Gu Shusen, Director Li Zheng, Counselor Yang Fang, and Counselor Chen Shizhen were appointed to assist Director Xin Shuzhi of the Compilation and Examination Department (who was later appointed Director of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau after the Compilation and Examination Department was merged into the Bureau) to jointly plan and organize the first China Education Yearbook Compilation and Examination Committee to oversee all compilation and examination matters, and to set up a compilation office responsible for drafting manuscripts. Thus, on April 25, Director Xin Shuzhi, Director Zhang Xiushan, Director Guo Xinsong, Director Gu Shusen, Director Li Zheng, Counselor Yang Fang, Counselor Chen Shizhen, Counselor Chen Panzao, Counselor Wu Chuzhou, Secretary Gan, Secretary Liang Jikang, Section Chief Zhang Fanjiu, Section Chief Xie Shuying, Section Chief Guo Youshou (later appointed Specialist), Section Chief Dai Yingguan, Section Chief Wu Yanin, Section Chief Zhong Lingxiu, and Section Chief Peng Baichuan, Section Chief Wang Ruiyuan and other nineteen people were appointed as compilation and examination committee members, with Director Xin responsible for convening meetings. Zhou Shuxian, Wang Fengtong, Gong Zhengtao, Ke Shuping, Qian Wangjunzhuo, Gao Weichang, Wu Yonglong, Huang Longxian, Cai Yuxin (deceased) of the Higher Education Department, Zhang Weigao, Wang Wanzhong, Weng Zhida, Chen Zhe, Xue Tianhan, Huang Wenqi of the General Education Department, Gu Liangjie, Guo Lianfeng, Jin Guisun, Shu Chushi, Gao Hongtu of the Social Education Department, He Bolie of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department, Xue Quanzeng of the Examination Department, Li Yiyan, Hu Yanli, Zhou Qidong, Huang Shuzhong, and Ding Zhiping of the Compilation and Examination Department, and Zhou Bangdao and other twenty-eight people were appointed as compilers, and Zhou Bangdao was appointed as the chief compiler. Later, due to slight changes in the Ministry's personnel and many official duties, Gao Tinzhi, Shen Pengfei, Zhang Jiong, Section Chief Qiu Changkang, Specialist Cheng Qibao, Specialist Yang Lian, Specialist Li Ximou, and Specialist Li Jiaxiang were successively appointed as compilation and examination committee members, and Zuo Zhong, Zhao Huang, Li Gongming, Ding Yizhong, You Chunmao, Fan, Mai Guoren, Li Guanglie, and Li Jingyao were appointed as compilers. In October of the 21st year, Huang Wenqi was added as the deputy chief compiler. In addition, Tai Shuangqiu, Luo Tingguang, Zhu Baoqin, Jin Zhaojun, Shen Zishan, Zheng Hesheng, Zhang Qiuxi, and Yang Kejing were specially invited as compilers by the Compilation and Examination Committee. This is a general overview of the assignment and invitation of colleagues in the first China Education Yearbook project.

The content of the compilation was initially drafted as a catalog by Chief Compiler Zhou Bangdao, and then the Compilation and Examination Committee made additions and deletions based on the opinions of various departments, and finally decided to divide it into five sections: Section A, General Overview of Education; Section B, Educational Laws and Regulations; Section C, General Situation of Education; Section D, Educational Statistics; and Section E, Educational Miscellany. Each section is further divided into several chapters and sections. The reason why it is called the first China Education Yearbook is that our country has never had a national education yearbook before. This compilation is indeed a pioneering effort. Except for the laws, regulations, general situation, and statistical facts, which are based on more recent materials, the rest mostly start from the late Qing Dynasty and end in the present. It is difficult to clearly delineate the years. Moreover, our country has a vast territory, inconvenient transportation, and policies are often hindered. It seems not easy to compile a volume annually in the shortest possible time to provide for the people of the country. It took some hesitation to adopt the term "first". However, to be accurate, it would be more accurate to call it "A Brief History of Modern Chinese Education, Volume 1."

The nature of education yearbooks published in Europe and the United States differs, including international, national, educational administrative organs, and academic research institutions. The formats vary, including reporting general situations, discussing issues, publishing monographs, presenting research results, and recording educational laws and regulations. The nature of this yearbook belongs to the national educational administrative organs, and its format focuses on reporting the general situation, supplemented by the recording of laws and regulations, and attached with the presentation of research results. As for the longitudinal narrative of educational facts, such as the sections on educational purposes, school systems, and educational administrative organization in Section A, the sections on general overview of higher education and general overview of secondary schools in Section C, and the sections on major events in education since the rise of education, the general situation of the publication of textbooks, and biographies of pioneers in education in Section E, each topic explores the origin and purpose, forming its own system, which can be said to be the original format of this yearbook.

The sources of materials for this yearbook can be roughly described as follows: First, the facts filled in by various educational administrative organs, consulates, schools, and academic research institutions and organizations according to the survey forms; second, the old and new archives of the Ministry; third, the publications of various educational administrative organs and academic research institutions and organizations; and fourth, the books and newspapers published by various associations and bureaus on educational facts. The first type is the most basic element. The various divisions formulate the matters to be submitted in all aspects and attach survey forms with outlines of the general situation, etc., and on May 3 of the 21st year, they issued an order, specifying the staff to fill in accurately item by item. Due to the staggered submission of reports from various provinces, the printing was delayed until the end of January this year.

The overall review of the manuscripts for this yearbook Section A and Section E were the responsibility of the former Compilation and Examination Department, special topics were written by specially invited compilers, Section B was the responsibility of the Counselor's Office, Section C's general overview of higher education, study abroad, and academic research institutions and organizations was the responsibility of the Higher Education Department, Section C's general overview of secondary education, elementary education, and overseas Chinese education was the responsibility of the General Education Department, Section C's general overview of Mongolian and Tibetan education was the responsibility of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department, and Section D was the joint responsibility of various departments. The article on social sports in Section C was reviewed by Mr. Hao Shisheng and Mr. Wu Yunrui because it belonged to a specialized field. This was based on the principle of division of labor and cooperation.

Regarding the drafting, receipt, and registration of yearbook documents, Zhou Gan of the Committee and the Secretariat initially handled them conveniently, and then the Compilation and Examination Committee designated Zhou Gan of the Committee and Zhou Bangdao, the chief compiler, to jointly be responsible, and specially set aside a collection of reference books and newspapers for the reference of the compilers. The secretaries were responsible for distributing the materials submitted and writing the completed manuscripts. Later, Chief Compiler Zhou had to go out to inspect schools due to his duties and could not be in the Ministry full-time, so all matters were presided over by Deputy Chief Compiler Huang Wenqi.

During the compilation process, colleagues talked about it afterwards and felt that there were many shortcomings. The main ones were: First, the reference years of various general situations were not consistent, and they could not be consistent due to the source relationship. Second, the materials sent by various parties were uneven, and the prescribed items for various general situations were often not fully prepared, and there was no basis for them, so there were many omissions. Third, the organization of the Compilation and Examination Committee and the establishment of the compilation were not very unified and coordinated, and there were practical inconveniences. Fourth, the members of the Compilation and Examination Committee and the compilers held concurrent positions, and they could only engage in this work when they had time after completing their own duties. Their spirits could not be focused, and efficiency was inevitably reduced. Fifth, the compilation staff were busy with official duties and had little time to gather and discuss, and the style and format, details and priorities were each determined by themselves. The facts are there, and there is no denying it. Sixth, only by not forgetting the past can we be a teacher for the future. The second and subsequent education yearbooks will be better than the first, which can be asserted.

Colleagues Zhong Shuyu, Wang Jiaxu, Fan Wenying, and Zhou Yunshang in the Ministry, whether checking files or collecting records, did not hesitate to be meticulous and provided a lot of assistance. Secretaries Yuan Rangguang, Yang Shiwei, Zhuan Ruomei, Xie Yulong, Shen Cheng, Tao Yuying, Wu Zengqi, Liu Yu, Zhang Guangxin, Sheng Xixi, He Xinhang, Duanmu Guangtao, and Lu Yanzi worked successively and tirelessly. Also, Zhang Aoshan proofread the entire book for punctuation and symbols. Recently, Chief Compiler Zhou had to travel to Henan and Shanxi, and Sun Shao伯 worked with Deputy Chief Compiler Huang to compile and proofread the book for printing, which was also laborious. All of these can be recorded.

The Case of the Qixia Monk and the Qixia Rural Teachers College is Not Yet Settled 218

Before the 15th year, Qixia Temple was deserted. After that, the person in charge changed, the monk was good at socializing, and he carried out large-scale construction to make it焕然一新. Qixia Rural Normal School was established in front of the temple, and the monks and Confucians each went their own way, originally井水不犯河水. However, the temple believed that the surrounding area of the temple was large in ancient times because it checked the local chronicles, and that the location of the school and even the surrounding residential houses and fields belonged to the temple property in ancient times. Although there were reasons to use ancient laws to judge the present, it was difficult to prove the facts. Because of this view, local people and monks had opinions from time to time. The monk in charge of the temple did not come forward, but Monk Jiran (this monk is like a staff member in an institution, not a leader who negotiates with people. Lawsuits were filed, and the struggle was fiercest in the 17th year of the Republic of China. Huang Zhifu, the principal of Qixia Rural Teachers College, was sued by Jiran to the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Education, and the General Headquarters that year, but none of them were successful. Then he filed a lawsuit in the Jiangning Local Court, and appeared in court many times. The court ruled that Huang was not guilty and decided not to prosecute, and the Jiangsu Department of Education issued an order to inform Qixia Rural Teachers College. However, because Monk Jiran was fond of litigation and made false accusations, the local people filed a complaint with the Jiangning County Government and had a public order to expel Monk Jiran from the country and not allow him to stay in Qixia Temple again. Several years later, Monk Jiran recently sued Huang Zhi in the local court, but none of them were successful. Then he pointed out witnesses for the excavation of graves and filed a public prosecution with the court. In addition, there were many tourists to the famous Qixia Temple. The monks in the temple have always complained to the dignitaries of the temple. The dignitaries listened to one side of the story without careful investigation and were deceived by the monks. Some came forward to intercede. (In the 17th year, a certain Minister of Agriculture and Mining issued a letter to the Ministry of Education through the mountain after listening to the words of the monks during a temple tour, ordering the rural teachers to protect the ancient sites. Later, Principal Huang submitted a document explaining that a certain Minister understood. Recently, a certain member and two院長, etc., jointly sent a private letter to the provincial authorities. Although it has been explained, most of the dignitaries understand, but Huang Zhifu has been affected by the judgment.) It is heard that the Jiangning Local Court has sentenced Huang Zhifu to eight months in prison, and the education community feels injustice for Huang. In addition, due to the face of a certain dignitary, mediation is underway and reconciliation is in progress. Huang is still appealing according to law, but the order to go to Japan to study education has been carried out. It is heard that the Director of the Jiangsu Education Department has sent an official document to the High Court explaining that Huang has gone to Japan for study, which will last for three months. During these three months, please slow down the progress of this case.

Alumni Association of Zhonggong Graduates Appeals to the Nation for the Rejuvenation of the Alma Mater 227

Painfully Recounting the Past Tragic History and Mission

Hoping that the Nation Will Respond with Justice and Material Assistance

Since the resignation of Principal Xiong Kewu from China Public School, school affairs have long lacked a person in charge. For the sake of maintaining the school and their own studies, the students of the school organized a petition group to request the school board, including Yu Youren, to select a principal and revitalize school affairs. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that the Alumni Association of the school has specially issued an appeal to the nation yesterday for the rejuvenation of the alma mater. The original text is as follows:

Appeal to the Nation: Our Zhonggong was established to resist the oppression of Japanese imperialism, and it was also destroyed to resist the oppression of Japanese imperialism. Is the spirit of struggling against adversity only the glory of our students? Since the January 28th Incident, although there has been no shortage of people who care, there have been few who have inquired about its restoration, causing a school with nearly thirty years of glorious history to decline from here. Can we not feel pain? Our graduates cannot bear to sit idly by and watch the demise of our alma mater. Therefore, we will briefly describe the past history and mission of our China Public School to inform the nation:

Pioneer of Anti-Imperialism: 1. China Public School was the pioneer of anti-imperialism for the Chinese nation. In the thirty-first year of Guangxu, Chinese students studying in Japan returned to the country in anger and founded China Public School to oppose the newly promulgated regulations restricting students in Japan. It started the beginning of our Chinese people's establishment of universities. The meaning is profound, and the achievement is especially great. 2. At that time, except for the two or three schools run by churches in the country, there was only the Imperial University of Peking affiliated to the autocratic government. The feudal traditions were deep, and the supervision was especially strict. Party members could not stay. Therefore, although there were revolutionary plans, there was ultimately a lack of a venue for mobilization. Our Zhonggong arose in time, and party members such as Mr. Zhang Binglin, Dai Jitao, Yu Youren, and the late martyr Chen Yingshi, etc., were stationed there for a long time, laying the foundation for the revolution under the name of teaching. Hundreds of students were filled with revolutionary sentiments. Therefore, during the Guangzhou uprising in Xinhai, when the Premier left Shanghai, he landed at Wusong Dunhui and asked the alma mater for funds. The school authorities immediately assisted with a fund of 3 million to continue the revolution. After the establishment of the temporary government in the two capitals, the temporary Senate settled the Qingyuan Yin Tong's debts to the government. The China Public School Fund was reported below. Sun Yat-sen, Huang Kunqiang, and Mr. Song joined the board of directors. It can be seen that in those days our Zhonggong served the party with meritorious service, and that our party was mindful of Zhonggong.

Spirit of the Martyrs: 3. China Public School proclaimed for the party. Under autocratic rule, the people of the country regarded it as a monster, a bandit, and slandered it, causing trouble for the future of the school. The general manager, martyr Yao Hongye, Mr. Hongye, lamented the hesitation of the people of the country, resented the decline of the nation, and angrily committed suicide by jumping into the sea. His last words were thousands of words, dripping with beauty, saying, "My death is for the death of China Public School." Also, Mr. Zhang Bangjie, the director, died of exhaustion while supervising the school building. All of these two gentlemen sacrificed for Zhonggong. Therefore, the existence of Zhonggong for one day means that the spirit of the martyrs is not dead for one day.

Destroyed in a Flash: Alas, Zhonggong had the mission of anti-imperialism, possessed the glory of revolution, and was finally destroyed by violent Japan. Our government even ordered it to close within a limited time, which is what our students would like to hear, and what the people of the country would like to see. Yao, the martyr, said, "China Public School is a touchstone for the ability of the Chinese nation. If it cannot be established and developed, it is also a representative of the inferiority and defeat of the ability of our people." Students, people of the country, can we also be willing to be representatives of the inferiority and defeat of ability?

Plan for Rejuvenation: This association bears the trust of our graduates. At this time when the alma mater lacks a person in charge and is on the verge of life and death, how dare we remain silent? In addition to urging the board of directors to quickly plan for rejuvenation, select a principal with both talent and ability to preside over the school, and petition the government to withdraw the order to close within a limited time, in order to maintain our country's glory and the alma mater for the survival of the nation, we hereby say auspicious words, hoping that the nation will respond with justice and material assistance. Zhonggong is fortunate, Shenhua is fortunate.

Hangzhou Art School Holds Exhibition in Shanghai 228

Date: March 3rd to 9th of Next Month

Lin Fengmian and Others Have Come to Shanghai to Arrange

The National Hangzhou Art School will hold an exhibition at the Sino-French Friendship Association at No. 11 Huanlong Road in Shanghai from March 3rd to 9th, every day from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM. (V) Italian Vocational Education 233

Since 1928, Italian vocational education has been uniformly managed by the Ministry of Education. The Ministry of Education has established the Department of Arts and Crafts Education as a specialized agency, assisted by the Second and Third Subcommittees of the Supreme Education Committee. Each subcommittee is organized by seven members, with a total of fourteen members in the two groups. Part of the members are selected from scientists and technicians, and part are selected from agricultural, industrial, commercial, and nautical experts. The committee is composed of people from the two departments. In terms of supervision and guidance, the Ministry of Education relies entirely on the Royal Inspectors, the Local Arts and Crafts Education Committee, and the School Management Committee to cooperate in handling all affairs.

(1) Classification of Vocational Schools: Italian vocational schools can be divided into the following three categories: 1. Preparatory schools and preparatory classes for agriculture, industry, commerce, and navigation; 2. Vocational schools for agriculture, industry, commerce, and navigation; 3. Arts and crafts schools. In the earliest period, the academic level was very uneven, and the names were also different. After three decrees in 1928, 1929, and 1932, the teaching programs were unified and standardized. However, there is still no obstacle to the students' further education and the flexible development of each school due to special local conditions. There are now three types: three-year preparatory schools, and two-year and one-year preparatory schools. There are 486 royal secondary vocational preparatory schools, 255 two-year classes, and 409 one-year classes.

Agricultural Schools: Although agricultural education in Italy developed very early, the specific organization only began 45 years ago. At that time, the government began to establish practical agricultural schools and specialized agricultural schools, mostly established by local authorities and assisted by public groups. There are 27 practical agricultural schools and 7 specialized schools, with a secondary level of education, with a course of study from three to four years, mainly to cultivate the children of middle-level small-capital farmers. Among the specialized schools, four focus on grape cultivation and winemaking, one focuses on rural industries, one focuses on apples and horticulture, and one focuses on animal husbandry and cheesemaking. Although most schools can strive for progress with the changes of the times, agricultural science is developing extremely rapidly, such as new methods of cultivation, livestock improvement, selected planting and fertilization, the application of agricultural tools and machines, and the prevention and treatment of plant diseases and animal diseases. All of these require rich knowledge and a considerable scientific foundation to cope with. In order to remedy this, the Italian education authorities reorganized agricultural schools in 1923, with the following aspects as the entry point for rectification: (1) stipulating the scope of secondary agricultural schools, (2) increasing the level to meet the needs of agricultural engineering, (3) designating the specialties that each school should offer, and (4) expanding the budget of each school to meet new needs. The school level is also determined according to the level and the needs of each place, and there are the following levels of schools:

Royal Secondary Agricultural Schools: These are national schools, and the salaries of teachers and staff are borne by the government. However, the local and central governments share the daily maintenance costs equally. Each school has a farm for practice and experimentation. The internal administration is presided over by the school affairs management committee. Students admitted to the school must be between the ages of 13 and 17 and have completed four years of middle school. The course of study is three years for the general course. Those who are interested in further study may enter the fourth year of the specialized course, such as grape cultivation, apple cultivation, horticulture, cheesemaking, olive tree cultivation, oil production, winemaking, animal husbandry, and mountain forest economics.

Registered Secondary Agricultural Schools: There are not many of this type of school. So far, there are only two schools that have been registered and recognized as being equivalent to Royal Secondary Agricultural Schools.

Practical Agricultural Schools: There are currently eleven schools of this type. The course of study is three years. Only those who have graduated from elementary school can enter the school. The government provides an annual subsidy. The Roman Practical Agricultural Machinery School is known for its short-term training nature, specializing in teaching the application of rural machinery, and graduates in March.

Girls' Agricultural Schools: This type of school mainly teaches courses such as home economics and rural work. The government provides an annual subsidy.

Arts and Crafts Education 234

Arts and crafts schools are places for training skilled workers in handicrafts and machine manufacturing. Schools are divided into three levels. The first level is worker schools, with a three-year course. The second level is apprentice schools, which train applied technology and manufacturing workers, with a three-year or four-year course. If there are special classes attached to train specialized technologies, they may be called senior arts and crafts schools. Apprentice training may also focus on one subject and shorten the training period to one year. This type of school is called factory schools. The third level school is the national arts and crafts school, which is of a higher level and is a place for training senior technical personnel in various industries.

Private arts and crafts schools that are recognized by the government are given a certain amount of subsidies annually. Girls' arts and crafts schools mainly focus on subjects such as clothing sewing and cooking.

At present, there are 11 national arts and crafts schools, 60 apprentice schools, 11 short-term specialized apprentice schools, 50 factory schools, 13 girls' arts and crafts schools, and 4 mining schools nationwide. The annual fee for national arts and crafts schools at all levels is 42.3 million Italian lire (1930-1931 budget), and the subsidies for private schools are not included.

Sports News

Hubei Provincial Department of Education Prepares for the Fifth Central China Games 235

Postponed for Three Years Without Being Held

Now Planned for Mid-May in Wuchang

(Hankou Correspondence) The Fifth Central China Games was originally scheduled to be held in Hankou in the 20th year of the Republic of China and was organized by the former Hankou Municipal Bureau of Education. Later, the meeting was moved by the Provincial Department of Education. A preparatory committee was established, and an organization budget book was drafted, including the meeting period expenses and the repair of public sports fields, with a planned cost of more than 177,700 yuan. It was submitted to the provincial government meeting for discussion and approval. At that time, due to the severe flood in the province, it was ordered to be postponed to the spring of the 21st year. Since then, although the Department of Education has repeatedly proposed holding the games, it has repeatedly ordered to reply due to the provincial treasury's shortage of funds. It was scheduled to be held in the spring of the 22nd year, but Li's headquarters ordered a temporary postponement. As a result, the meeting has been postponed for more than three years and has not yet been held. Xu Qibao, director of the Department of Education, believes that in order to develop national sports and increase interest in sports, it is necessary to unite the provinces of Central China to hold competitions. The meeting seems to be impossible to delay any longer. It was submitted to the Sports Committee of the Department for discussion on the 15th of this month. It was decided to hold the games in mid-May. According to Article 7, Paragraph 6 of the Constitution of the Central China Sports Federation, a preparatory office should be organized three months before each games and notify the provinces. Now that the time is pressing, a preparatory committee should be established immediately to plan everything. In terms of funding, in addition to the preparatory expenses, the repair of the sports field, the expenses during the meeting period, and the expenses for this province, the travel, board, and lodging expenses of the athletes and staff of other units, as well as other miscellaneous expenses, should be borne by the respective units to save money. As for the location, both Wuchang and Hankou are acceptable. However, Wuchang is the seat of the provincial government, with many schools and convenient participation for athletes. The original provincial public sports field has hosted the Third National Games and the Seventh National Football Regional Games. The scale is rough and repairs are easy. Both time and expenses are more economical. The above proposals were submitted to the Provincial Government Committee Meeting on the 10th. It was decided to approve the establishment of a preparatory committee, and the location of the games will be determined according to the equipment of the sports fields in Wuhan, with different types of events. The required expenses will be discussed by the Department of Education in a drafted budget.

Maritime Basketball Supremacy Changes Hands, Mai Ling Defeats Pirates Again to Win the Championship 237

Shanghai Basketball Group A Second Final

Mai Ling Wins Again with 45-32

Average Talent is Key to Mai Ling's Victory

The Shanghai Basketball Association Group A Championship has shifted this year from the Pirates to Mai Ling. In the second final last night, Mai Ling defeated the Pirates again, with a score of 45 to 32. From then on, the supremacy of maritime basketball was declared to have changed hands.

Fierce and Terrifying 238

The intensity and ferocity of the game was terrifying. Both sides acted brutally, almost engaging in hand-to-hand combat. Although there were many fouls, the referee did not enforce the rules strictly enough. Some players almost resorted to violence, creating a tense atmosphere. One can imagine how fierce it was. The Chinese team is no match for them, and even the North China team may have difficulty winning. This shows how quickly Westerners' basketball skills are improving, while the Chinese are not making progress. This year's International Games may not be interesting to compete in.

Comparison of the Two Teams 239

Mai Ling's victory was due to its strong and well-rounded team. The team's talent was evenly distributed. The six forwards were all equally good, and the guards were also solid. In the Pirates' team, since Si Lei was unable to attend due to injury, the defense was weakened. The substitutes were not up to par. Smith's weakness detracted from the team's performance, and the forwards also suffered a lot. Although Xiao Shiguiya and Bian Ersheng fought hard, they had to succumb to their opponents. On the other hand, Mai Ling's movements were exceptionally quick, and their shooting accuracy last night seemed as if the ball was connected to their heads.

Difficult to Separate 240

At the beginning of the game, Tui Lu and Locke each missed a good opportunity to score. Rhein scored first, and Shi Guiya made a free throw. The Pirates took a 3-0 lead. Mai Ling did not show any weakness and followed closely behind, trailing by only one or two points. Eventually, with a goal by Luo Ai, Mai Ling took an 11-1 lead. Da Shiguiya made adjustments, and the Pirates regained the lead. Near the end of the first half, Mai Ling suddenly gained momentum and scored four consecutive points, taking a 22-20 lead for the first time.

Pirates Fall Miserably 241

In the second half, the Pirates returned to the court with the same lineup as before. Mai Ling continued to press forward relentlessly, and their momentum was terrifying. The Pirates had difficulty developing their offense, and the situation became increasingly bleak. Mai Ling increased their lead from 26-20 to 30-23, leading by seven points. The Pirates' energy declined further, and their formation became disorganized. At 40-30, the outcome of the game was completely decided. The final score was 45-32, and Mai Ling won the championship.
