Spring and Autumn

The Art of Living 249

— Jin Zi

If this title were translated into classical Chinese, it would naturally be "Secrets to Getting Along in the World," but those four characters seem too old-fashioned. Writing them out would definitely not have any appeal. Therefore, the author has no choice but to imitate the old shop with a new opening method and use a different title.

Before discussing "The Art of Living," the author must first make an algebraic formula so that readers can understand it more clearly.

"The art of living is not general, but changes with the environment and time."

Therefore, the art of living we are discussing here is really just the art of living for a modern Chinese person. The applicable time may be ten years, maybe one year, or maybe just a few months. In short, when China's politics are on the right track and China's society stops being disturbed, the lives of all these arts of living can be declared over at the same time.

In the past, people didn't talk about the secrets of getting along in the world, but when they did talk about them, it was always about flattery and bragging. In fact, those things are no longer applicable. Now, only three characters are applicable: "ruthless," "clever," and "fast."

Ruthless In this world, although we cannot openly eat people raw or kill people casually, we cannot be too timid or too compassionate. As long as it is beneficial to yourself, you can ignore the lives and deaths of others and do whatever you want. If you feel that someone is hindering you, you should immediately take action to remove him and must eradicate him completely, so that he has no chance of revenge. In short, your gut must be as hard as possible, and you must not care about heaven, reason, or human feelings. Only then will you have food to eat!

Clever Flattery and bragging were originally the most brilliant art of being Chinese. Now, because there are too many people who can flatter and brag, they are no longer very effective. But if you can use your ingenuity and think of a clever way to flatter and brag, you can still exchange it for foreign money!

Fast This character is the most important. If you only have a "ruthless" gut and a "clever" mind, but you don't have "fast" means, you will definitely not be able to stand on your feet in China in these years. Even if you can stand on your feet, you still can't escape being bullied, scolded, and starving. Because now the entire society of China has become a world of grabbing food, and you must always talk about taking the initiative first. You must always keep the mentality of running a 100-meter race and compete with others. Then, even if you can't get much advantage, you will definitely not suffer too much!

Hobbies 250

— Zhou Limin

The term "hobby" refers to all aspects of a person's interests outside of their occupation.

There are many types of hobbies, such as drinking, playing cards, smoking, calligraphy and painting, watching movies, and collecting antiques. Chinese people often warn people to curb their hobbies, but I think there is much room for discussion.

People in this world really do not live for survival. We "cherish life and fear death." What we cherish is not life, but the various satisfactions and enjoyments that life gives us. What we fear is not death, but the deprivation of various satisfactions and enjoyments after death. Therefore, the more ways a person feels interested in the environment, or we can say the more hobbies they have, the richer and more meaningful their life will be, and the more unwilling they will be to abandon life.

Therefore, negative people, misanthropes, and suicidal people are probably interested in only one aspect and lack hobbies. Because they have no other hobbies besides their own job, no family joy, and no friendship with friends, and they do not feel interested in their own job, life is of course meaningless.

When a person is in love, life has meaning, and it is for the sake of their lover. Life and love become one and two, and two and one. Unfortunately, when they are lovelorn, life loses its meaning, they become misanthropic, and they commit suicide. That is the process that many young people who commit suicide because of lovelorn go through!

Therefore, if ordinary people are too focused on one aspect and completely abandon and isolate other aspects, they will be in danger of becoming negative, misanthropic, and suicidal when they are frustrated in the aspect they are pursuing.

From a psychological point of view, hobbies should not be curbed, but should be cultivated in many ways. Hobbies that are beneficial to the body and mind are worth promoting.

Warm Quilt 251

— Xu Xiaoting

The cold wind is freezing, and the climate is freezing. People abide by the ancient training of "working at sunrise and resting at sunset." In this winter, no matter how cold the climate is, they always have to get up and work, eat and drink, in order to seek a comfortable life for the day. Winter is the hibernation period for animals. Humans are endowed with active bodies and agile minds, and they cannot endure hunger and cold, so even in the icy and snowy environment, their hearts are still active, and their bodies are still stirring.

The winter wind cuts like a knife on people's bodies, and the winter climate surrounds people, with no warmth at all. After asking about the cold and working hard all day, people's only comfort is the warm quilt they wrap themselves in at night. Eight hours of work, eight hours of rest, and eight hours of sleep. The quilt is a warehouse where people store their bodies. In winter, people see the value of a warm quilt as a mysterious, warm, enjoyable, and memorable palace of pleasure.

The necessary items for the organization of a warm quilt are the quilt and mattress. According to the minds of knowledgeable humans, this minimum level of enjoyment can of course be enjoyed by everyone in the human living environment. But understanding is understanding, and facts are facts. On this winter night, the quilts of the rich are soft and warm, and the quilts of the poor are stiff and cold. Warm quilts are really a special product enjoyed by the rich. The bodies of the poor can only squat in ice-cellar-like burlap bags and paper tubes made of advertising paper.

The most enviable warm quilt is the young men and women, the newly married young couples. They wrap themselves in it, whispering sweet nothings and showing their affection for each other. They simply regard the warm quilt as a mysterious magic palace. But looking back at the flood victims along the Yellow River, in this winter, they have no cotton clothes to keep out the cold during the day and no cotton quilts to wrap themselves in at night. They are really unable to enjoy the warm quilt!

We are in this ice-cellar-like winter night. Frost is spread all over the ground, and the wind is shouting for people. Among our 400 million compatriots, are there more people sleeping in warm quilts or fewer people sleeping in warm quilts? I'm afraid there is no need to ask a statistician. We can guess it. Therefore, "Behind the vermilion gates, meat and wine go to waste, while on the road lie frozen corpses." Wearing burlap bags and covering themselves with paper, those who freeze to death have short lives, and those with long lives can never die.

Proof of Kerosene Curing Lung Disease (Part 2) 253

— Bing Yu

I immediately refuted them one by one based on facts and reasons, saying, "Talking about the advantages and disadvantages of kerosene is entirely a matter of dosage. For example, morphine and aspirin, etc., will also cause danger if taken in excess. Kerosene is originally a safe and non-toxic substance, hundreds of times safer than spirits and liquor. There are many materials that can prove the safety of drinking kerosene in certain quantities from an academic and experimental perspective. If you think it violates morality, please point out the harm." That doctor dared not make any further defenses. This is a great shame for the medical community, calling himself a doctor but not knowing enough about kerosene. In short, kerosene is effective for all types of lung disease. However, why is it effective? Because kerosene contains special ingredients. The separation of these special ingredients will provide clinical experiments for medical researchers, and there should be a detailed explanation and publication. As for the method of drinking, according to my experience, try drinking 5 grams for the first time. After three or four days, drink it again. If diarrhea, vomiting, headache, fever, and other reactions occur after drinking, stop temporarily. If there are no side effects, increase the dose to 1.2 grams and drink it once every three or four days. The time to drink is on an empty stomach before going to bed. The maximum dose is 20 grams for early-stage patients, 15 grams for stage-one patients, and 7.5 grams for those with hemoptysis or stage-three patients. Pay close attention to the time of drinking and the number of days of separation. Ordinary small doses have the same properties as Chinese rhubarb and can be used as a stomachic. It is difficult to cause diarrhea or a rise in body temperature after drinking, but it is temporary, so don't worry about it. Drinking it will definitely increase appetite and make you feel refreshed. It is also okay to use it with other medicines. As for the type of kerosene, ordinary kerosene for lighting is fine. It is best to use oil with a slightly yellow color and 0.4% impurities. High-quality kerosene is not suitable for drinking.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 254

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 25 Tearful Farewell to Loved Ones, Hastening Home to Guard the Border, Wind and Sand Throughout the Night, Leaving the Village to Station in a Lonely City

"Oh God, let the light in, let the lover out." This folk song has been popular since ancient times and is so sad. But when it came to Yang Guizhi, it was not letting her lover out, but urging her husband, who had not been married for long, to go far away. It was not only sad, but simply miserable. So when Zhao Ziqiang said he was leaving, Guizhi grabbed Ziqiang's hand and couldn't speak for a long time. Ziqiang whispered, "Don't be sad. I'll write to you as soon as I get to the front. I'll find a house in a nearby village. Let's live there comfortably. What do you think?" Guizhi said, "That's naturally good, but this matter is not important. I hope you will be careful in everything." Ziqiang shook her hand, unable to say anything else. Just then, they heard the door of the opposite room creaking. Zhao Weng was already shouting in the living room, "Ziqiang, are you up?" Ziqiang immediately opened the door and came out to greet him, saying, "Dad, I'm up." Zhao Weng said, "I heard you two talking all night. Didn't you sleep?" Ziqiang said, "In that case, you probably didn't sleep either?" At the same time, there were messy footsteps in the yard. Jiang Shi said outside with a trembling voice, "Are you all up? Has Ziqiang's luggage been checked?" Guizhi quickly opened the door of the living room and said, "Mom didn't sleep all night either." Ziqiang smiled and bowed to Jiang Shi, saying, "The old lady also got up so early." Everyone was talking, standing in the living room, without knowing what to do, as if everyone had some kind of illness in their hearts, just panicking. Guizhi was still clearer-headed. First, she took Ziqiang's watch and put it in his pocket. Then, she put the checked suitcase and leather bag on the chair in the living room. (323)

A Bottle's Journey 259

A Greek man in Athens, how pleased he must have been when his daughter, seriously ill, miraculously recovered! When his daughter fell ill, he vowed to donate five silver dollars to a monastery. He was a poor man, and these five dollars represented his entire fortune. Instead of sending the money through the post office, he placed it inside a glass bottle, wrote a note of thanks for the answered prayer, and threw it into the sea. The bottle crossed the Mediterranean, floated on the surface, and eventually landed seven miles from Allanc-Saint-Dad, reaching the shore. The money arrived at the monastery, and the bottle is now on display in the local museum.

Free Talk

The Philosophy of Mahjong 261

— Meng Zhen

Aside from Mei Lanfang, mahjong is probably the only aspect of Chinese civilization that has been successfully promoted overseas.

Why is mahjong so popular? Because within these 136 tiles lies the philosophy of Chinese life. The three words "pong," "chow," and "hu" truly explain everything in our human world.

The most important thing when playing mahjong is to be able to pong pairs and chow sequences. Then, you are very likely to hu. Chinese life is the same: as long as you have good luck and seize opportunities skillfully, you can rise from a clerk to a chairman, from a stable boy to a military governor. If you win the lottery, not only can you easily gain fame and become a celebrity, but it will also be easy to become a chief or director of something. Therefore, the most important thing for the Chinese is destiny. Divination and astrology may be criticized as superstition, but they are still popular in society, revered by everyone from important party and state figures to cart drivers and coolies.

However, although we talk about destiny, human effort is also relevant. When luck is on your side, anyone can hu a pure hand with three doubles. But when luck is against you, even a skilled player can minimize their losses. Therefore, while believing in destiny, we also say that humans can conquer nature.

Moreover, in eight rounds of mahjong, winning and losing often fluctuate, creating a rollercoaster of emotions, making people happy and angry, forgetting everything. Throughout it all, people hold onto a hope: the hope that the winner can win even more, and the hope that the loser can break even. This is like people's attachment to life; no matter what, they are unwilling to give up their will to live and commit suicide until they are completely hopeless.

In a society where some people can enjoy the best living conditions with no skills, simply by chance, while others, despite their talents, live in poverty, the game of mahjong is undoubtedly a very apt representation. In reality, all social relationships are already fixed. The talk of fate or the idea that humans can conquer nature is nothing more than a way to eliminate the consciousness of struggle and maintain the stability of the existing society. Because if we talk about human conquest of nature, old and unreasonable systems can be broken by human effort. However, in mahjong, you can never escape the control of luck. So, although we talk about human effort, everything is still entirely dependent on fate.

Mahjong originated in China under the rule of the leisurely feudal class and became popular in the United States under the rule of the leisurely capitalist class in the 20th century. This has its reasons because the difference between China and the United States is merely that one is at the highest stage of feudal exploitation and the other is at the peak of capitalist exploitation.

A Tragic Comedy (Continued) 262

— Shi Heng

He proceeded according to his plan. In less than three months, almost every family in this small town had someone sick in bed. It could even be said that everyone in the town was ill. The only inn in the small town, which used to have very little business, now had no empty rooms. It was completely full of patients, and the inn had become a hospital.

Three months later, Dr. Palpare, who had previously given Croque this territory, came back to the small town to collect his debts. His surprise was extraordinary. But Croque dispelled his surprise with just a few words of explanation. Palpare understood the logic, but his conscience could not accept it. Thus, the author created the following dialogue:

Palpare: If I had your method, if I really had this method like you... if I had this ready-made method that I could just put into practice...

Croque: I understand.

Palpare: Wouldn't I feel any unease? (Silence) Please answer me.

Croque: But I think this is something you should answer yourself.

Palpare: You see, I'm not explaining anything. I'm only picking out the most euphemistic point.

(Silence)

Croque: I don't quite understand what you're saying.

Palpare: You'll definitely say I'm too strict, too meticulous. But in your method, isn't the patient's interest somewhat predicated on the doctor's interest?

Croque: Dr. Palpare, have you forgotten that there's an interest higher than both of these?

Palpare: What interest?

Croque: The interest of medicine. That's the only interest I'm dedicating myself to.

Next, Palpare asked him: "But you can't put the whole town in bed!" He wiped his hands and said, "There's still room for discussion on that. Because I've personally seen a family of five, all sick at the same time, all in bed, and they're coping very well..." From this, we can understand how sufficient this doctor's reasons are!

Perhaps some people will doubt whether this doctor is real, but to me, he couldn't be more real. The doctors we usually see are somewhat like this Mr. Croque. However, this Croque, who appears on stage, is too aware of himself. He analyzes all his actions clearly, while most doctors in the world are not so consciously aware. He can say out loud that he is for the "victory of medicine," while many doctors, although they believe and practice in the same way, don't even understand it themselves. Although Palpare can say, "Isn't the patient's interest somewhat predicated on the doctor's interest?" he hasn't actually been any different in practice. It's just that he doesn't have Croque's talent. Isn't that a good proof? He's immediately going to switch places with Croque, he's willing to give up his position in Lyon and come back to this small town.

The most crucial part of the whole play is in the dialogue quoted above. Both doctors' faces become serious, and the reader and audience can no longer laugh. It points out a truth that we usually overlook, and we remain helpless even when we understand this truth; at least until there is a fundamental change in this society, there is nothing we can do.

After reading this play, like after reading "The Tale of How Ivan Ivanovich Quarreled with Ivan Nikiforovich" or "The True Story of Ah Q," I was left with a heavy heart, more so than the power given by any tragedy. That's why I call this play a "Tragic Comedy."

Wine of Tears 263

— Ye Rong

Yi Hong slightly opened her lips and poured a cup of wine straight down. It cut through her throat like a sharp knife, causing her to choke uncontrollably. The guests laughed, and the sisters laughed too. She felt her face burning, and her throat continued to sting.

"Another cup!" The fat man raised a full cup of wine and shouted. His face, pushing against the layers of fat, was as red as burning coal, glowing. He brought the wine straight to Yi Hong's lips, breathing heavily through his nose.

She hurriedly pushed it away, but he kept pushing it forward, saying, "You have to drink... you have to." Everyone clapped and shouted, some even leaving their seats and running over. Yi Hong looked at everyone with a mournful face. The guests were getting excited, and the sisters were watching on the sidelines with bitter smiles. She had lost all help, like a lamb in distress, almost wanting to cry.

The fat man also squinted, holding up the cup. Wine spilled from the cup, which trembled in his hand. "Drink, you can drink Lao Zhang's wine, you can drink mine too. Drink, you have to drink."

It felt like a fire was about to erupt in her heart. She wished she could punch those squinting eyes. But she turned her head and didn't move. She felt tears welling up in her eyes. But she immediately remembered what her madam had said, that she had to treat her smiles as her tears. So, she desperately held back. She felt dizzy and unsteady, and she sat down with a slump.

Someone came over and said nice things, but the fat man didn't agree. A large, rough hand covered in blue veins reached over and turned her face around, and the wine poured down her neck in an instant. She heard a clanging sound in her ear as the wine cup shattered on the ground.

She woke up as if from a dream, humiliation immediately biting at her heart. She jumped up, ignoring the cold wine that was pouring down her neck straight to her heart, and turned to leave. She felt her limbs trembling. But as she took a step, she was grabbed.

"Leaving? You have to drink even more. See where you can go."

The fat man was panting, holding her shoulder tightly with one hand, gripping it painfully. His eyes were bloodshot, like an angry beast. Yi Hong felt like her whole body was on fire, and she forgot everything. She raised her hand and struck the fat arm hard, and the fat man's hand tightened, then suddenly laughed.

"Good, you hit well." He shouted, raising his other hand high, a huge, rock-like fist suspended in the air. The guests and sisters crowded around. Immediately, countless hands reached out, pulling and tugging. Yi Hong seized the opportunity to break free, and four greyish-white finger marks were clearly visible on her bare arm.

In the midst of the chaos, Yi Hong was dragged down the stairs. She heard the sound of broken bowls and dishes upstairs. She got into a rickshaw and fled into the brightly lit streets. She felt dazed and confused, not knowing what she had done tonight. Tears fell from her face like broken beads, and she forgot everything. She still had the wine stain from just now on her cheek...

Random Notes on Returning Home 264

— Gao Zhi

Before returning home, I passed through Nanjing and took the Nanjing-Wuhu long-distance bus. Buying the ticket and getting on the bus were both disorderly and crowded. From the company's perspective, this shows that public institutions are not handling things well, selling as many tickets as possible without considering the congestion after passengers get on the bus. Some people even swayed for several hours without a seat, and their backs couldn't straighten when they stood. On the way, I saw children throwing stones at the bus. The bus had to cross the river by ferry, which was time-consuming and laborious.

I took a walk on the streets of Wuhu and saw many people who didn't look like beggars but were wearing clothes that weren't too tattered, who had come from the countryside to the city to escape the famine and beg for food. I heard the workers on the road saying, "Things in the countryside are really terrible, getting worse every year."

There was a small steamboat from Wuhu to Chaoxian, and I happened to encounter "shared trips." A single trip ticket cost four dimes, while a shared trip ticket cost two dimes. The ticket price was the same regardless of the length of the journey. When there were no "shared trips," the customs on this route were considered among the worst of the small inland river steamboat routes on the Yangtze River. The "connecting river" phenomenon of monopolizing cabin space and the company's free pricing both inconvenienced passengers. Everything seemed disorderly and unregulated. To see more, I also sat in the large passenger cabin. I heard many passengers say, "A person who never leaves home is a noble person." The inconveniences experienced by passengers on the Yangtze River where boats travel can be seen here. Of course, there was also the "pushing and shoving" phenomenon on the large Yangtze River steamboats. There were quite a few opium smokers on the boat. The true "masses" in the cabin talked about stories from heroic chivalry tales. They probably wouldn't read new literature for another twenty or thirty years. This is a matter of fact, unrelated to pleasant theories.

I stayed in a lodging house (i.e., a hotel) in Chaoxian for three dimes a day, and there was also a meal of ten dishes, which was really cheap and good. But the market conditions were more than twice as desolate as they were eleven years ago. After another hour by bus, I arrived home. Both the bus and the road were bad. The road passed over a small mountain top, and it was said that the reimbursement for opening this mountain top was 100,000, but in reality, the cost was limited, and the entire route was built by farmers contributing labor, without receiving a penny in wages, similar to the new style of "agricultural corvée" when building the Great Wall. How the reimbursement was done is difficult to know for sure. This is also one reason why people want to become officials.

At home, I had the opportunity to contact various people and review the situation in the interior, seeing the reality of people's lives in a broken-down rural area. They have no education; nineteen out of twenty are illiterate. They have no money; nineteen out of twenty are in debt. They want to celebrate the Lunar New Year. I vaguely know why it's difficult for them to improve their lives and why the so-called lords above want to exploit them. Some people have great difficulty borrowing a dollar to buy rice for the New Year's Eve dinner, and it's hard to sell a rooster on the street to get money for the New Year. Some have to travel hundreds of miles to Wuhu to pawn things (pawnshops in small cities don't open, for many reasons), but some are unfortunate enough to encounter bandits on the way, and these bandits all have modern weapons. Yet, they want to celebrate the New Year, burn incense and paper money, smoke cigarettes, light kerosene lamps, and eat foreign sugar. Looking at the commercial situation in one district of one county alone, kerosene and cigarette stores can earn more than 50,000 yuan a year, but the real earners are not Chinese, and the consumers are mostly farmers. Local products are worthless, rice doesn't sell for four yuan a picul, and peanuts sell for two or three yuan a picul. How can farmers live like this! Looking at a small town with a population of just over 10,000, there are 200 opium dens, full every night. Various shops have little business in the twelfth lunar month, but opium dens are as prosperous as ever. Therefore, ordinary people see the importance of black rice (opium) as no less than that of white rice (food). In ordinary families, offering opium is the same as offering cigarettes, a matter of social etiquette; otherwise, it is disrespectful and loses face. There are signs on the thoroughfares saying that those who grow opium will be executed, but there are formal "soil shops" (opium dens) in the area.

I went to Hefei once. The situation in this area is similar. The countryside is declining, and everyone is struggling, but the emaciated farmers have to carry the fat lords and watch them play all kinds of civil and military tricks. Many village women and children are born strong and intelligent, but like the men, they have no education and will all become illiterate. Even uneducated, local corrupt officials who haven't read foreign books can control these ignorant poor people very well. I dare not expect any hope for this society. In the interior, people celebrate the Lunar New Year, paste door couplets, and set off firecrackers. The result of the New Year is the addition of many bankrupt large and small shops and countless unemployed shop assistants and workers. The countryside cannot accommodate them, and the cities cannot accommodate them either. The nice talk is "immigration," but it is not known if there is really any place to move to. They also cannot take turns going on stage to collect some money and live their lives, so everywhere they cry out in poverty.

Mary Marchinaf's Diary (3) 265

— Translated by Ye Zi

Two days later丨Otter asked me for a souvenir. I gave him a pin from my hat. But he liked my diamond hairpin. I understood his hint. I am his most precious person, just as the diamond is the most precious of my possessions.

X X X X X X X

This morning丨Yesterday, Otter asked me for another souvenir. I took out a gold coin and asked him to break it in half. Otter didn't want to. I guessed his thoughts. He was afraid that this would break our love. He hid the whole gold coin, expressing that our love is one. How clever that thought is!

X X X X X X X

The next day丨I just gave him another gold coin. He exchanged a copper Kopek with me. I understood again. Our love will always be as pure as gold and as strong as copper.

I'm afraid Alexi will come back, and I'm afraid Otter will kill him.

X X X X X X X

Later丨I told Otter about Alexi. I said I was his fiancée. At first, Otter didn't answer at all. He was afraid that he would not be able to contain his anger. Later, he packed up his painting tools, preparing to leave. Then, I told him that Alexi hadn't come yet. Otter was finally quiet and took out his paintbrush again.

X X X X X X X

Three days later丨Alexi will be here in half a month. I told Otter that we should commit suicide. Our love demands it of us. Otter suggested that I commit suicide first, and then he would starve to death in front of my grave.

### Demand for Foreign Loans is Starting to Stir 269

|Foreign Call Loans Still Offered at Interest-Free Rate|

Yesterday, although the banking and money shop sectors were still quiet and indifferent towards the foreign exchange situation, the demand from various commercial sectors gradually started to grow, resulting in an overall thriving atmosphere. Foreign call loans were still being offered at the interest-free rate in the market, primarily because of excessive overnight funds, resulting in continuous weakness. Overnight clearings at the Small Bankers' Association were done at the interest-free rate. The volume of transactions in call loan notes was over 2 million in the early morning and over 300,000 in new transactions. Transactions at the Small Bankers' Association totaled over 500,000. Foreign mortgage loan transactions involved redeeming 300,000 to 400,000 and making 500,000 in new loans. Over 1.1 million in banknotes were collected and issued. Customer traffic was approximately 400,000. Bank receipts and payments: foreign banks received and paid over 1.2 million in bills, over 3 million in various goods, foreign exchange mortgages, and miscellaneous receipts and payments, and over 1.2 million in settlement receipts and payments, with 200,000 going into storage. Chinese banks received and paid over 2.5 million in bills, over 3.5 to 3.6 million in various goods, foreign exchange mortgage taxes, and miscellaneous receipts and payments, and over 1.3 million in settlement receipts and payments, with 400,000 going out of storage. Japanese banks received and paid over 2 million in bills and over 1.7 to 1.8 million in various goods and miscellaneous receipts and payments, with 300,000 going out of storage. ### Securities - April Futures of Public Bonds Debut 271

Restoration of Four Sessions of Trading Per Day

Various Bonds First Rose Then Showed Discrepancies

Prices Have Reached a Peak, Both Bulls and Bears are Cautious

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange began trading April futures and restored the four sessions of trading per day, both morning and afternoon. Due to the two-day market closure for the weekend and settlement, the environment was favorable. The Sun Chuanfang disturbance had been resolved, and the issue of rising silver prices was not expected to have any immediate impact. Speculators covering short positions and large investors buying caused market prices to rise again, reaching a peak. Market sentiment was excellent, with a tendency to discover new high prices. At the opening in the morning, short positions in the Thirteenth issue were covered, and there was considerable buying in the Fifth issue. Buying also exceeded selling in the Fifteenth issue. In general, retail buying was also strong, but the Northern group sold slightly, causing market prices to uniformly increase by one or two jiao to about four jiao. In the second session, buyers continued to surge in, and the trading floor was extremely tight, with prices rising another three to five jiao. Almost all the losses from the previous Saturday had been recovered. Investor confidence was strong, and market sentiment was good. In the two afternoon sessions, the market became slightly chaotic, with prices fluctuating up and down, and the range of price changes being small, generally between one and three jiao. In general, however, there were more rises than falls, and the trend may temporarily stabilize and then move upward. The final results for the day showed that prices rose between one or two jiao and about one yuan, with the 1920 Customs Bonds and Salt Tax Bonds showing the largest increases of nine jiao and nine and a half jiao, respectively. Although the April futures were opening for the first day, only the 1918 Customs and Gold Long-Term Bonds did not open for trading. The rest opened across the board, and prices were also good. The total number of transactions was 14,150,000 yuan. There were no spot transactions. ### Only 9,200 Bales of February Auction Yarn Were Delivered 276

|The Price was 181 Yuan|

February auction yarn was launched on September 1 of last year, with an opening price of 187 yuan and three jiao. Subsequently, due to the slump in the U.S. cotton market, the decline in China's rural economy, and the sluggish sales of spot yarn, the market gradually trended weak. Then, on October 16, the National Economic Commission established the Cotton Industry Control Association, which implemented plans to maintain yarn prices. Market prices saw a slight increase, until changes occurred in the Fujian-Zhejiang military situation in November, and a certain factory was unwilling to take delivery, causing prices to fall again. In mid-December, the lowest price was seen outside of 172 yuan, before negotiations between India and Japan on the cotton industry were successfully concluded at the beginning of this year. Indian cotton rose sharply, and cotton prices followed suit. The Shenxin factory, seeing the rising cost of raw materials, became increasingly difficult and firmly maintained yarn prices, buying heavily in the auction yarn market. The market suddenly rose sharply, extending to the last session of the month at 181 yuan and five jiao, an increase of 11.5 yuan compared to the previous month's price. As a result, 9,200 bales remained, and it was reported that Yong'an delivered 2,800 bales of Jin Cheng yarn, 2,000 bales of 20s Fuguai yarn, 50 bales of 20s Zhinu, and 50 bales of Tianguan. ### Grains: A Large Decline in Futures Flour, Followed by a Small Rebound 279

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, market conditions for all months generally presented a sluggish and listless appearance. Quotations for foreign wheat, Chicago were down by a small three or four jiao, and Canadian were down by a small eight fen or so. Therefore, at the time of opening, near-term market sentiment was seen to be flat. The opening price was as low as 2.065 yuan, down by more than one fen from the previous day. March through June were also seen to be weak at the same time, while July remained stable. When the afternoon session opened, only half a day of trading was left for this month. Initially, conditions were still flat and weak, but then a general short covering gradually compensated. Fuxin chips were also being withdrawn. Therefore, the opening price rose step by step, and distant-month contracts were also slightly rebound as various factories stopped and outside investors made slight inroads. This situation is still a small rebound from a large decline, and the future still holds little hope. With the tracking activity of spot foreign wheat, domestic real sales are also difficult to achieve smoothly. It is feared that it will remain weak and spiritless afterward. As a result, this month rebounded by one fen compared to the previous day, March rebounded by 1.25 fen, April rebounded by 1.75 fen, June rebounded by 1.5 fen, and July rebounded by 1.75 fen.

### 18 Cars of Futures Wheat Were Delivered 280

Yesterday was the delivery of February futures wheat, and the futures market was closed. ### Ke Xian Rice Sales are Turning Active in Local Markets 281

Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice market saw a slowdown in Min-Yue [Fujian-Guangdong] dealings, but sales were concentrated on local streets. The flow of goods in transit was not large, and the market stabilized. Sales opened at 3,200 bags of Ke Xian at various stalls, with prices not differing significantly from the previous day. However, due to slight differences in the quality of the goods, the selling prices also varied. Yesterday, Ke Hua was only inquired about by the Fuzhou group. Other groups were all in wait-and-see mode. The Fuzhou group purchased 1,400 to 1,500 bags, and the rest were all taken in by local streets. In addition to receiving machine-milled Ke Xian at a price of Ke Yuan, local streets also received 200 bags of re-inflowed small-grain rice at a price of 6.85 yuan, the same price as the previous transaction. There were no orders for foreign rice, which has been in short supply for a long time, and only inventory remains. Because foreign merchants are unwilling to let go of the product easily because of high costs, the rice market is temporarily supported and must await inquiries from major groups after the Lantern Festival before it can turn for the better. However, it is said that once sales are strong and market prices rise, rice will be transported from the production areas to Shanghai, so it will not be easy to have a very good market afterward.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Thoughts

The Tide of Suicides Among Young Women 308

— Chen

Suicide among young women, which was once sporadic, has gradually become more frequent and widespread. Around the New Year's Day on the lunar calendar, it almost reached its peak. It is unknown how many troubled and distressed young women are about to embark on this path of "great rest" to seek great liberation from life. If we do not casually regard this fact as a "minor matter" for "water-cooler talk," we will notice its severity. This is undeniable: suicide among young women is no longer an accidental event to be excited about; it has, in fact, become a widespread phenomenon that numbs the mind. However, it is a trend that cannot be taken lightly.

Even when the early spring festival drums were urging the Lunar New Year, there was the student Hu Zhen, who committed suicide because she was not admitted to the school she applied to, and the teacher Huang Shan, who harbored "pessimism" because his salary was in arrears and he was insulted and dismissed. During this joyous Spring Festival, when every family was raising their cups and drinking longevity wine, it was even more a time to "start anew with the year," and the situation intensified. First, there was the film star Ai Xia, who gained great fame in society for starring in "A Modern Woman," who took her own life by swallowing opium. Then, there was the young Miss Yan, who was abandoned by her fiancé and sought redress in the afterlife. And the famous courtesan Li Wen suddenly took her own life. Although these people who "rashly took their lives" were of different categories and different qualities, they were all young women. Suicide by young women, and the social nature that suicide manifests before our eyes, is the same.

The reasons for these young women's pessimism and suicide are that some have experienced all the hardships of life and deeply feel the economic oppression; some yearn for the ivory tower of "love above all else" and suddenly encounter the disappointment of disillusionment; some admire the vanity that can make women proud but cannot find it; and some have experienced the world and cannot escape the dangers and deceit of society and people's hearts. In any case, if we do not imitate the attitude of journalists to get to the bottom of things and pursue the facts, we can synthesize a fundamental question of why these women commit suicide and why it has become a "fashionable" trend.

The current so-called new slogans of "women's liberation, equality between men and women, and freedom of marriage" are concealing a lot of "freedom" to play with and enslave women when "equality, freedom, and liberation" cannot be achieved among people within society, especially among some "modern" young women who are proud of themselves. Because the so-called "love" nowadays is completely equal to a Yuan silver dollar engraved on "lace" in an environment where money is omnipotent. With it, there is "love"; with it, no amount of "deep affection" exists. Under this "truth," many sons and wealthy men whose ancestors were virtuous use the power of money to carry out a large-scale purchase of "love"; and many "modern" girls also dream of marrying a "golden turtle." But since there is "love" with money, after asking about it several times and promising oneself in body, how can one guarantee that they will follow each other for life and not be discarded like worn-out shoes? This makes many young women who are full of dreams of being a wife and grandmother inevitably suffer "abandonment" and "heartbreak." However, the allure of cars and foreign houses ultimately makes ordinary "modern" women yearn for them, which makes many women who lose this dazzling expectation inevitably become "pessimistic."

Even so, there are still many enthusiastic young women who dream of finding a lifelong companion with deep affection in this social arena; it's just that such "Camellia" girls rarely encounter the "Armand" of the time, making them deeply feel that the "love scene is full of illusions" and have no desire to live, so they abandon the world and kill themselves. As for many women who have not competed in this "love scene" and are destined to become mechanical slaves, although they may not commit suicide in despair of life, they are forced to embark on a path of chronic suicide.

The inability of women to be economically independent drives them to increasingly flaunt "modernity" and auction off "love," which repeatedly leads to abandonment, heartbreak, and suicide. At the same time, in a society where money buys love, it creates their extreme "vanity," but they always feel "disillusioned." Naturally, this phenomenon will intensify with the deepening of the economic panic, causing young women to embark on the "tide" of suicide. If women's economic independence and the system that prevents women's economic independence do not change, I am afraid that the suicide of young women will become a serious problem that is "flourishing" and "getting worse."

A Record of the Second Public Performance by the Shanghai Nameless Drama Actors Association 309

— Xuefei

Recently, the Shanghai Nameless Drama Actors Association held its second public performance of spoken dramas at the Lakeside Society on the 26th of this month to support unemployed workers and the rent reduction movement in Shanghai. There were two performances, day and night. I went to see the night show, which consisted of the following four acts: (1) The Vagabond, (2) Brothers, (3) One Hundred Pounds, (4) Living Together in Three Families. The first five acts of the four acts were probably foreign scripts, while the last act, "Living Together in Three Families," was newly written by themselves. Its content depicts the pain of the recent Shanghai rent burden.

Among the four acts, the one that won the most applause from the audience was "One Hundred Pounds." The content of this act is roughly as follows: "On the bank of a river in Ireland, a British police chief waits for an escaped revolutionary, hoping to capture him and exchange him for a reward of one hundred pounds. But the Irish revolutionary is not like the one depicted in the reward notice. Another poor singer plays a six-stringed lute and sings moving songs, warning him that he is the person he wants to catch. However, with his wit, he not only avoids the police chief's suspicion but also persuades him to escape from his grasp. 'A hundred pounds reward, a hundred pounds!' The police chief asks himself empty-handed if he is a fool." (According to the program notes). The plot is also very ordinary, without much twist, but the performance of the actors is excellent. Especially the dialogue, every sentence is powerful, every sentence is humorous, it is really wonderful to the point of perfection, there is not a sentence that does not have a very profound meaning. Listening to it is like drinking mellow wine, like reading famous verses, one only feels refreshed and everything is possible. This is naturally because the script was originally written well, but the fact that the actors were able to perform it appropriately made the essence of the whole play completely revealed without any omission. We see how much extremely profound and rich poetic meaning is contained in his (the actor's - the poor singer's) every move, every word. His clothes are extremely tattered, his face is dirty, and his legs are spread apart, but at the same time, his words are satirical, his actions are strange, and at the same time, it can be said that he is unconstrained and transcendent. Furthermore, we can also see that the passion in his heart is particularly unrestrained, and his thoughts are extremely calm. Ah, what a lovable person this is! No matter how ugly his appearance is, we only find him lovable. Not only lovable, but when compared with the noble and decent gentlemen, young masters, ladies, and young ladies, we only feel that the rest of the decent people are not like people, and only this ugly singer is the only true person! What a profound and powerful satire this is! The actor has grasped this profound and powerful satire completely and presented it to the audience without missing a single detail. I think, although I am a layman when it comes to drama, the audience cannot but say that this act was very successful.

Secondly, "Laure" in "The Vagabond," "Chen Guiqing" in "Living Together in Three Families," and "Su Wei's Mother" also each had considerable success in their performances. The actor who played Laure portrayed the typical egotistical of the general petty bourgeoisie (although Laure is a worker, he is a foreman, and his consciousness is petty bourgeois, and he used to be a running dog of the capitalists) to the point of being extremely meticulous. Chen Guiqing in "Living Together in Three Families" was drunk and adorable, and his words and actions were very humorous. Su Wei's mother was a living, ignorant old woman. I don't know how the actor was able to portray her in such a strange and interesting way. The tone was like a painting, and it was really a credit to the actor for being able to think of it and do it.

Looking at the plays as a whole, although there are many loose and rough spots, we can be very satisfied with this achievement.

A few days ago, we had almost no plays to see. Movies are either just lively and prosperous or their content is completely distorted. It is rare to have such a public performance of spoken dramas, which provides us with some spiritual food. Although its content is not necessarily very progressive, it is still good. Therefore, in the end, I hope that the progressive drama circles in Shanghai will have the opportunity to give us a few more public performances.

Come Back, My Child! 310

— Bo'er

In the quiet garret, you could hear the clock next door striking five. Wasn't it so? Another day had passed like this, and the few small coins in my pocket had been spent like this. Getting up early every day, sitting tightly in front of the desk, holding a pen, I really don't know what to write. Writing some articles can be sold for some money to maintain life and remedy your unemployment period. This temporary way of life seems easy, but it also seems very difficult. Looking at me today, with my head down, sitting for a day, I don't know if I wrote a dragon or a tiger? I feel very tired myself, and my head also hurts. I thought I had to run outside to change the air.

It was just in the fifty minutes between my going out and coming back, these hateful fifty minutes. When I just stepped into the alley, the little maid A Dou ran to the road in a panic. She passed in front of me but didn't see me. I thought she was rushing to buy things to cook, so I casually called out to her: "A Dou! Where are you going?" When her eyes turned to my face, she grabbed my clothes, knelt on the ground with both feet, and shouted: "It's not good! Younger brother is gone! It was just for a moment! It's not good, where can I find him?" She said and stood up again, turned to the police, and knelt down again, using the same anxious tone to ask him for help. The police officer may have had too much experience and was used to people losing their children. He was not sympathetic. He calmly said: "Then you should look around! Who told you not to be careful?"

When I saw this situation, I was already numb. He was lost, he was taken away, how could I find him back? My heart was panicking and aching, but I didn't cry. I quickly jumped into a rickshaw and drove straight to the Yokohama Bridge District Office. The person sitting in the office asked me to fill in a form after opening a notebook. After I wrote my name and age, I began to seriously question him: "If I write like this, can you find my child back? Other people's lost children can be found, right? Or not? What method will you use to help me find him? Aren't you going to hurry up? Why are you sitting still? I must find him!" Regardless of what answer he gave me, I was extremely anxious and only knew how to ask him. The person in the office thought I was too strange. He was conscientious and finally promised that I could make a phone call to other district offices to teach them to pay more attention to me.

"Pay attention! Is paying attention enough? If I had money, if I threw my banknotes on your table, then couldn't you grab the swindler at the train station, on the road, at the street corner, or anywhere else? Get my child back? Forget it! Even if my child is sent to someone else from your hands, do you think about how he will cry tonight? How will he look for his mother? Is paying attention enough? Good sir!" This crazy shouting made the office man stand up angrily and slap the table. He wanted to argue with me. I remember that there was a person wearing a military uniform next to me. He persuaded him and sent me out the door. At that time, my tears rolled down from my deep eyes.

Sitting in the rickshaw, it pulled me home. Many women were standing at the door, discussing, but they didn't actually help me find him. They just talked. I couldn't help but hate them. I regretted going out for a walk just now, and I hated the article I wrote even more. How much money can it sell for? My child is lost, what is the price? Ah! Maybe he is being hidden in the room next door, but as long as someone intends to do evil, then even if we are in the same Shanghai, on the same road, or even in the same alley, we are still forever separated. He is calling for his mother, and he cannot hear his mother's response. How pitiful he is! I don't understand why people want to make him lose his mother's love and snatch him from my arms? Even if he can be sold for money, how much is he worth? Twenty yuan? God knows! A pair of ladies' silk stockings hanging in the company's glass window are not also marked at twenty-odd yuan? ...

Come back, my child!

Brother Mao and Sister Bao Travel the World 311

— Meng

Novel

Husband and Wife (10) 312

— Yu Mei

The third girl woke up when she heard footsteps outside the wall. She poked her head out of the quilt, lifted the curtain, and saw a glimmer of white light through the cracks in the closed wooden window. She shrank back into the quilt and pressed her naked hot body a little closer to the man.

The man's fatigue had not yet recovered, and his breathing was still even. The third girl licked his lips and jaw, but he was still sleeping soundly. The third girl stroked him for a while, afraid of waking the man, so she first left his body and put on her shirt. She heard that there were already many pedestrians outside.

She went to the water boiler to rinse water, washed her face, and also woke the man up. The man was putting on his clothes. She prepared the wash water and put it on the table. She put a piece of cloth from the bed into the compartment under the cabinet, and smiled silently at the man, implying something.

There were footsteps outside, and her husband was back. She hurriedly went out and saw that her husband's hands were empty, but she was a little surprised that there was a smile on her husband's face. She asked,

"Did you bring back the tobacco ash?"

"I forgot." The man smiled.

"Go and get it quickly, I'm going to cook the opium soon, there's not enough ash at home."

Xu San went with another kind of joy. The man in the room was buttoning his clothes while saying he was leaving.

"Haven't you washed your face?"

"I'll wash it when I get back. I'll send the fabric when I have time." The man smiled and went out the door.

She stood outside the door and watched him walk away. The mud on the street had all frozen into a layer of black ice, and there were still piles of snow by the wall, with a layer of black ash on top. The snow in the tile gutters on the roof opposite was white.

When Xu San walked into the room with a smile holding the tobacco ash, her dissatisfaction with her husband was not as great as it was last night. Xu San handed the tobacco ash to her and seemed particularly gentle. He sat on the edge of the bed and asked,

"Is your head still hurting?"

"I slept all night, and it's much better."

Xu San slowly took out a five-yuan bill and two yuan from his purse.

The third girl asked in surprise: "Is it the money for the opium?"

"No, I haven't sold half of the opium yet. There are still people smoking."

"Then where did it come from?"

"I picked it up."

"Where did you pick it up?"

"I picked it up under the table leg in the gambling house."

"Was it last night or this morning?"

"It was in the middle of the night."

"Fortunately, I asked you to sell the opium, so you made some extra money. We're bound to have good luck this year."

"I'm exhausted. You can take this money first. I want to sleep for a while."

"Okay, you sleep."

"You stay with me."

"I stay with you? Won't you cook the opium?"

"Let's cook the opium tomorrow." Xu San said, taking off his shoes.

"That's right, I haven't weighed enough opium yet. Let's borrow two taels from Xiaoyuzi's house this afternoon and add them to cook."

(The End)
